Answer: Return value from @Test method captured via ITestContext or instance variables set in @BeforeMethod. Or use ThreadLocal shared context. Avoid static shared mutable state in parallel runs.

Interviewer expects: ITestContext or ThreadLocal approach.

Q62: What is IMethodInterceptor?

Answer: intercept(List<IMethodInstance>, ITestContext) reorders or filters test methods before execution. Sort by priority, custom logic, or runtime conditions. Returns modified method list.

Interviewer expects: Dynamic test ordering.

Q63: How do you disable tests based on environment?

Answer: IAnnotationTransformer checks environment property and sets annotation.setEnabled(false) for tests not applicable to current env. Or use group exclusion in environment-specific testng.xml files.

Interviewer expects: Dynamic enable/disable pattern.

Q64: What is configfailurepolicy?

Answer: Suite attribute: "skip" (default) skips all tests when @BeforeSuite/@BeforeTest fails. "continue" attempts remaining tests despite config failure. Choose based on whether config failure makes tests meaningless.

Interviewer expects: Failure propagation control.

Q65: How do you integrate ExtentReports?

Answer: Create ExtentReportListener implementing ITestListener + ISuiteListener. Init ExtentReports in onStart, create ExtentTest per method, log pass/fail with screenshots, flush in onFinish. Register in testng.xml.

Interviewer expects: Full listener lifecycle.

15.3 Advanced Level (35 Questions)

Q66: Explain IRetryAnalyzer implementation.

Answer: Implement retry(ITestResult) returning boolean. Track attempt count, return true to retry, false to stop. Register via @Test(retryAnalyzer) or IAnnotationTransformer for global application. Manage instance state per test carefully.

Interviewer expects: Complete implementation with state management.

Q67: How do you apply retry globally?

Answer: IAnnotationTransformer sets RetryAnalyzer class on every ITestAnnotation in transform(). Register transformer as listener in testng.xml. All tests get retry without individual annotation.

Interviewer expects: Transformer + listener registration.

Q68: When should you NOT use retry?

Answer: Real assertion failures (bugs), tests with side effects (payments), performance tests, when failure rate exceeds 10%, data setup failures. Retry masks bugs and increases execution time without fixing root cause.

Interviewer expects: Critical judgment on retry misuse.

Q69: Explain IAnnotationTransformer for retry.

Answer: transform() method receives ITestAnnotation and sets setRetryAnalyzer(RetryAnalyzer.class). Called once per test method before execution. Enables centralized retry config, environment-based retry count, and conditional retry application.

Interviewer expects: Runtime annotation modification.

Q70: How do you ensure thread safety in framework?

Answer: ThreadLocal WebDriver, no static mutable state, unique test data per thread, independent tests (no dependsOnMethods in parallel), synchronized access to shared resources, separate Grid sessions per thread.

Interviewer expects: Comprehensive multi-point strategy.

Q71: Design a TestNG Selenium framework from scratch.

Answer: Maven project with TestNG + Selenium. Layers: BaseTest (driver lifecycle), Page Objects (PageFactory), Utils (DriverManager, ConfigReader, ExcelReader), DataProviders (external data), Listeners (ExtentReports, screenshots), testng-suites (smoke/regression). ThreadLocal driver, properties-based config, parallel XML.

Interviewer expects: Complete architecture with justification.

Q72: How do you handle dynamic elements in Page Objects?

Answer: AjaxElementLocatorFactory with timeout in PageFactory.initElements(). Explicit WebDriverWait in page methods. @FindBy with dynamic XPath/CSS. Avoid @CacheLookup for dynamic elements. Retry in wait utilities.

Interviewer expects: Wait strategy integration.

Q73: How do you implement custom HTML reporting?

Answer: Implement IReporter or ITestListener, collect ITestResult objects in a list during execution, generate HTML with pass/fail/skip counts, execution time, and screenshots in onFinish. Write to reports/ directory.

Interviewer expects: Result collection and HTML generation.

Q74: How do you integrate TestNG with Jenkins CI/CD?

Answer: Jenkinsfile with Maven test stage, testng.xml selection via profile, Allure/Extent report publishing in post-always, parallel stages for cross-browser, email notification on failure, artifact archiving of reports and screenshots.

Interviewer expects: Pipeline stages and report publishing.

Q75: What is @Factory with DataProvider?

Answer: @Factory method uses @DataProvider to return Object[] of test class instances with different constructor args. Each instance runs as separate test. Enables data-driven test class creation — e.g., different browsers or environments per instance.

Interviewer expects: Class-level data-driven pattern.

Q76: How do you handle stale element exceptions?

Answer: Re-find elements instead of caching. Use explicit waits with expected_conditions. Avoid @CacheLookup for dynamic pages. Implement retry wrapper in page methods. PageFactory re-locates on each access by default (without CacheLookup).

Interviewer expects: Re-locate strategy, not just retry.

Q77: Explain listener execution order.

Answer: Listeners execute in registration order for each event. IExecutionListener wraps entire run. ISuiteListener.onStart before ITestListener.onStart. Multiple ITestListeners fire sequentially. Exception in one listener may skip subsequent listeners for that event.

Interviewer expects: Event hierarchy and ordering.

Q78: How do you implement Page Object Model with TestNG?

Answer: Page classes with @FindBy elements and PageFactory.initElements(). Page methods return next page object (fluent navigation). Tests extend BaseTest, instantiate pages with driver, call page methods, assert in test class. No assertions in page objects.

Interviewer expects: Clean separation — pages act, tests assert.

Q79: How do you run tests in Docker containers?

Answer: Dockerfile with Maven + Java + Chrome. docker-compose with Selenium Grid (Hub + Nodes). CI builds image, runs mvn test with Grid URL. Parallel tests distribute across containerized browser nodes.

Interviewer expects: Container + Grid integration.

Q80: What is the difference between parallel="tests" and "classes"?

Answer: parallel="tests" runs each <test> XML block concurrently — ideal for cross-browser (each browser is a test block). parallel="classes" runs each Java test class concurrently — methods within a class remain sequential.

Interviewer expects: XML structure mapping to behavior.

Q81: How do you debug flaky tests in parallel?

Answer: Run sequentially first to isolate parallelism issues. Add thread-name logging. Check static variables and shared data. Reduce thread-count. Verify ThreadLocal cleanup. Use retry temporarily while investigating root cause.

Interviewer expects: Systematic isolation methodology.

Q82: How do you implement environment-specific testng.xml?

Answer: Separate XML files per environment with different parameters (URLs, credentials). Maven profiles select the file. CI passes -Denv=qa. Same test classes, different configuration — no code changes between environments.

Interviewer expects: Config externalization strategy.

Q83: Explain Allure @Step annotation.

Answer: @Step marks methods as report steps with auto-captured parameters and timing. Creates hierarchical report structure. Requires AspectJ weaver in Surefire argLine. Steps appear nested under test in Allure dashboard.

Interviewer expects: AspectJ dependency requirement.

Q84: How do you handle authentication in test framework?

Answer: Login once in @BeforeClass, store session cookie/token in ThreadLocal. Or API-based auth setup in @BeforeMethod. ConfigReader for credentials per environment. Never hardcode credentials in test code.

Interviewer expects: Session reuse and security awareness.

Q85: What is data-provider-thread-count?

Answer: Suite-level attribute limiting concurrent DataProvider iterations independently from thread-count. Useful when DataProvider has many rows but you want to limit browser instances to avoid Grid overload.

Interviewer expects: Fine-grained concurrency control.

Q86: How do you implement test retry with screenshot?

Answer: RetryAnalyzer for re-execution + ITestListener.onTestFailure for screenshot on each attempt. Track attempt via getCurrentInvocationCount(). Attach screenshots to ExtentReports/Allure with attempt number in filename.

Interviewer expects: Combined retry + listener pattern.

Q87: How do you measure test execution time?

Answer: ITestResult.getStartMillis()/getEndMillis() in listener. ExtentReports logs duration automatically. Allure captures timing per step. Custom listener can build execution time report. @Test(timeOut) enforces maximum duration.

Interviewer expects: Listener-based timing collection.

Q88: How do you handle file uploads in parallel tests?

Answer: Each thread uses its own test file copy (unique filename with thread ID). sendKeys with absolute file path. Clean up uploaded files in @AfterMethod. Avoid shared upload directory conflicts.

Interviewer expects: Thread-specific file isolation.

Q89: Explain ServiceLoader listener registration.

Answer: Create file src/test/resources/META-INF/services/org.testng.ITestNGListener containing fully qualified listener class names. TestNG auto-discovers and registers them. No XML or annotation needed — works across all suites automatically.

Interviewer expects: META-INF file format.

Q90: How do you implement database validation in TestNG?

Answer: DB utility class with connection from config.properties. @AfterMethod or test method queries DB to verify data changes. Use @BeforeSuite for connection pool. Clean test data in @AfterMethod. Thread-safe connection management.

Interviewer expects: DB utility + cleanup pattern.

Q91: How do you handle popup windows in framework?

Answer: Window handle utility: getWindowHandles(), switchTo().window(handle). BasePage method waitForNewWindow(expectedCount). Store original handle in ThreadLocal for return. Page objects encapsulate switch logic.

Interviewer expects: Utility-based window management.

Q92: What is the role of WebDriverManager?

Answer: io.github.bonigarcia.wdm automatically downloads and configures browser drivers matching installed browser version. Eliminates manual driver binary management. Called before WebDriver instantiation: WebDriverManager.chromedriver().setup().

Interviewer expects: Auto driver management benefit.

Q93: How do you implement API + UI hybrid testing?

Answer: REST Assured for API setup (create test data via API), Selenium for UI validation. @BeforeMethod creates data via API, test validates in UI, @AfterMethod cleans via API. Separate API utility class, shared config.

Interviewer expects: API setup + UI verify pattern.

Q94: How do you version-control testng.xml files?

Answer: Store in testng-suites/ directory in Git. Separate files per run type. Environment-specific parameters via Maven profiles or CI variables, not separate XML per env. Code review XML changes like code changes.

Interviewer expects: Git-managed suite configuration.

Q95: Explain TestNG XML suite file merging.

Answer: TestNG supports <suite-files> to include other XML files: <suite-files><suite-file path="smoke.xml"/></suite-files>. Combines multiple suites into one run. Useful for master suite orchestrating sub-suites.

Interviewer expects: Suite composition pattern.

Q96: How do you implement test prioritization in CI?

Answer: Group-based stages: smoke (5 min) → sanity (15 min) → regression (60 min). Fail-fast: smoke failure stops pipeline. IMethodInterceptor for runtime reordering. Maven profiles per stage with different testng.xml.

Interviewer expects: Pipeline stage strategy.

Q97: How do you handle TestNG with Spring Boot?

Answer: Use @SpringBootTest for integration tests with TestNG via spring-test dependency. @Autowired beans in test classes. @BeforeClass loads ApplicationContext. Combine Spring's DI with TestNG's execution control and reporting.

Interviewer expects: Spring-TestNG integration awareness.

Q98: What are common TestNG anti-patterns?

Answer: Static WebDriver, dependsOnMethods chains, hardcoded test data, assertions in page objects, shared mutable state, excessive retry masking bugs, one giant test class, no group organization, ignoring @AfterMethod cleanup, mixing unit and UI tests in same suite.

Interviewer expects: Recognition and alternatives for each.

Q99: How do you migrate from JUnit to TestNG?

Answer: Replace @Before/@After with TestNG equivalents. @Test import change. Convert @RunWith to testng.xml. Use TestNG assertions. Set junit="true" temporarily for coexistence. Migrate gradually — one module at a time.

Interviewer expects: Phased migration strategy.

Q100: How do you optimize a slow TestNG suite?

Answer: Enable parallel execution (methods or tests), use Selenium Grid for distribution, remove unnecessary waits, optimize @BeforeMethod (don't launch browser if not needed), group-based selective runs, headless browsers, retry only for known flaky tests, profile with listener timing data.

Interviewer expects: Multi-pronged optimization approach.

Section 16: Cucumber & BDD Introduction

What is BDD? (Behavior Driven Development)

Behavior Driven Development (BDD) is an agile software development methodology that encourages collaboration among developers, QA engineers, and business stakeholders by describing application behavior in plain, business-readable language before writing code or tests.

Core Idea: BDD bridges the gap between business requirements and technical implementation. Instead of writing tests in programming language syntax, teams describe what the system should do in a shared vocabulary that everyone understands — POs, BAs, developers, and testers alike.

Key Principles of BDD

  • Outside-in development — Start from user behavior and work inward to implementation.
  • Ubiquitous language — Use the same terms in requirements, tests, and code.
  • Examples over abstractions — Concrete scenarios clarify ambiguous requirements.
  • Living documentation — Feature files stay synchronized with actual system behavior.
  • Collaboration — Three Amigos (PO, Dev, QA) define behavior together before automation.

How BDD Bridges Business and Technology

Traditional testing often creates a translation gap: business writes requirements in Word/Jira, developers write code in Java, and QA writes test scripts in Selenium. BDD eliminates this gap by making Gherkin feature files the single source of truth that all three groups can read, review, and approve.

  Business (PO/BA)          Development              QA/Automation
  ─────────────────         ─────────────            ───────────────
  "User must login          LoginController.java     @Given user on login page
   with valid creds"   →   authenticate() method →  @When enters credentials
                                                      @Then sees dashboard"
         │                         │                         │
         └─────────────────────────┴─────────────────────────┘
                    Same Gherkin Feature File
                    (shared, readable, executable)

BDD vs TDD vs ATDD Comparison

CriteriaBDDTDDATDD
Full FormBehavior Driven DevelopmentTest Driven DevelopmentAcceptance Test Driven Development
Primary FocusSystem behavior from user/business perspectiveCode design via unit-level testsAcceptance criteria before development
Who Writes TestsCollaborative — PO, Dev, QA togetherDevelopers primarilyWhole team including customer/business
LanguageGherkin (Given/When/Then) — business-readableProgramming language (JUnit, TestNG)Natural language or Gherkin acceptance tests
Test LevelAcceptance / integration / E2EUnit tests (methods, classes)Acceptance / system level
DocumentationLiving documentation via feature filesTests serve as code documentationAcceptance criteria as executable specs
ToolsCucumber, SpecFlow, Behave, JBehaveJUnit, TestNG, NUnit, pytestCucumber, FitNesse, Robot Framework
When AppliedBefore/during feature development in Agile sprintsDuring every code change (Red-Green-Refactor)Before sprint starts — acceptance criteria defined
Stakeholder InvolvementHigh — non-technical stakeholders review scenariosLow — developer-centricHigh — customer defines acceptance tests
Best ForCross-functional Agile teams, E2E workflowsClean code, SOLID design, fast feedback loopsContract definition between business and dev
RelationshipExtends TDD to higher abstraction; often uses TDD internallyFoundation practice — BDD builds on TDD principlesConceptual predecessor — BDD formalized ATDD with Gherkin

What is Cucumber?

Cucumber is an open-source, Java-based BDD framework that executes plain-text specifications written in Gherkin syntax and maps them to executable step definitions written in Java (or other JVM languages like Kotlin, Scala).

  • Originally created by Aslak Hellesøy in 2008; now maintained by the Cucumber open-source community.
  • Supports multiple languages: Java, JavaScript, Ruby, Python (.NET via SpecFlow).
  • Integrates with TestNG, JUnit, Maven, Gradle, Selenium, RestAssured, and CI/CD pipelines.
  • Current stable version: Cucumber 7.x (JUnit Platform / TestNG integration).

Why Cucumber?

Business-Readable Tests

Feature files use plain English (or any natural language). A Product Owner can read Given the user is on the login page without knowing Java.

Living Documentation

Feature files describe current system behavior. When behavior changes, scenarios are updated — documentation never goes stale like Word documents.

Collaboration

Three Amigos sessions produce feature files together. Everyone agrees on behavior before coding starts, reducing rework and miscommunication.

Traceability

Each scenario maps to a user story. Tags like @JIRA-1234 link tests to tickets for audit and coverage tracking.

Cucumber Architecture

┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                        CUCUMBER EXECUTION FLOW                       │
└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

  ┌─────────────────┐
  │  Feature File   │  login.feature (Gherkin scenarios)
  │  (.feature)     │  Given / When / Then steps in plain language
  └────────┬────────┘
           │ parsed by Cucumber engine
           ▼
  ┌─────────────────┐
  │ Step Definition │  LoginSteps.java (@Given, @When, @Then methods)
  │  (Glue Code)    │  Maps Gherkin steps → Java/Selenium/API code
  └────────┬────────┘
           │ invoked by
           ▼
  ┌─────────────────┐
  │  Runner Class   │  TestRunner.java (@CucumberOptions)
  │  (Entry Point)  │  Specifies features, glue, tags, plugins
  └────────┬────────┘
           │ executed by
           ▼
  ┌─────────────────┐
  │  TestNG/JUnit   │  mvn test → AbstractTestNGCucumberTests
  │  Test Engine    │  Parallel execution, reporting, CI integration
  └────────┬────────┘
           ▼
  ┌─────────────────┐
  │  Reports        │  HTML, JSON, Allure, pretty console output
  │  & Hooks        │  @Before/@After for setup/teardown
  └─────────────────┘

Cucumber Dependencies for Maven

Add these dependencies to your pom.xml for a TestNG + Selenium + Cucumber project:

<properties>
    <cucumber.version>7.18.0</cucumber.version>
</properties>

<dependencies>
    <!-- Core Cucumber Java library -->
    <dependency>
        <groupId>io.cucumber</groupId>
        <artifactId>cucumber-java</artifactId>
        <version>${cucumber.version}</version>
        <scope>test</scope>
    </dependency>

    <!-- TestNG integration for Cucumber -->
    <dependency>
        <groupId>io.cucumber</groupId>
        <artifactId>cucumber-testng</artifactId>
        <version>${cucumber.version}</version>
        <scope>test</scope>
    </dependency>

    <!-- Dependency injection for sharing state between steps -->
    <dependency>
        <groupId>io.cucumber</groupId>
        <artifactId>cucumber-picocontainer</artifactId>
        <version>${cucumber.version}</version>
        <scope>test</scope>
    </dependency>

    <!-- TestNG -->
    <dependency>
        <groupId>org.testng</groupId>
        <artifactId>testng</artifactId>
        <version>7.10.2</version>
        <scope>test</scope>
    </dependency>
</dependencies>
Note: cucumber-picocontainer enables dependency injection between step definition classes without static variables. Each scenario gets a fresh instance of shared context objects.

Advantages of Cucumber (10+ Points)

  • Business-readable specifications — Non-technical stakeholders can review and approve test scenarios.
  • Living documentation — Feature files always reflect current system behavior.
  • Improved collaboration — Three Amigos sessions align PO, Dev, and QA early.
  • Reusable step definitions — Same step text reused across multiple scenarios.
  • Tag-based execution — Run smoke, regression, or sprint-specific subsets selectively.
  • Multiple report formats — HTML, JSON, JUnit XML, Allure integration out of the box.
  • Data-driven testing — Scenario Outline with Examples tables for parameterized tests.
  • CI/CD friendly — Integrates with Jenkins, GitHub Actions via Maven/Gradle commands.
  • Multi-language support — Same Gherkin syntax works across Java, JS, Ruby, Python.
  • Parallel execution — TestNG parallel DataProvider runs scenarios concurrently.
  • Hooks support — @Before/@After for setup, teardown, screenshots, and conditional hooks by tag.
  • Requirement traceability — Tags link scenarios to Jira tickets and user stories.

Limitations of Cucumber (5+ Points)

  • Abstraction overhead — Maintaining feature files AND step definitions doubles maintenance effort.
  • Learning curve — Teams must learn Gherkin syntax, Cucumber architecture, and DI patterns.
  • Performance — Slower than direct TestNG tests due to Gherkin parsing and step matching.
  • Over-engineering risk — Simple unit tests don't need BDD; forcing Cucumber adds unnecessary complexity.
  • Step definition sprawl — Large projects accumulate hundreds of steps; ambiguous/duplicate steps cause failures.
  • False sense of collaboration — If only QA writes feature files, BDD benefits are lost.
  • Debugging difficulty — Failures span feature file → step definition → framework code; stack traces are longer.

When to Use BDD vs Traditional Testing

Decision FactorUse BDD (Cucumber)Use Traditional (TestNG/Selenium)
Team compositionCross-functional with PO/BA actively involvedQA-only team writing automation scripts
Test audienceBusiness stakeholders review test scenariosTests are developer/QA internal only
Test levelAcceptance, E2E, API contract testsUnit, integration, performance, load tests
Documentation needLiving specs required for compliance/auditCode comments and test reports sufficient
Project typeAgile product with evolving user storiesLegacy system, API-only backend, microservices
Test complexityUser workflows with clear Given/When/ThenComplex data setup, performance benchmarks
Speed priorityReadability and collaboration over raw speedMaximum execution speed and minimal overhead
Maintenance modelShared ownership of feature files by whole teamQA-owned automation framework

Industry Adoption: Who Uses Cucumber and Why

Company / DomainWhy They Use Cucumber
Banking & FinTechRegulatory compliance requires readable, auditable test specifications linked to requirements
E-Commerce (Amazon, Shopify partners)Complex user journeys (checkout, payment, returns) benefit from business-readable scenarios
HealthcareFDA/HIPAA compliance needs traceable acceptance tests with living documentation
InsurancePolicy calculation rules expressed as Examples tables for actuarial validation
SaaS StartupsAgile teams use BDD for sprint planning and PO sign-off on acceptance criteria
Government / Public SectorProcurement requires documented test evidence readable by non-technical auditors

Interview Q&A — Cucumber & BDD Introduction

Q1. What is BDD and how is it different from TDD?

Answer: BDD focuses on describing system behavior in business-readable language (Gherkin) for acceptance testing with stakeholder collaboration. TDD focuses on writing unit tests in programming language before code, driven by developers for design quality. BDD operates at a higher abstraction level and often uses TDD internally for step definition implementation.

Q2. What problem does Cucumber solve?

Answer: Cucumber bridges the communication gap between business and technical teams. It allows requirements to be written as executable tests in plain language, ensuring everyone agrees on behavior before development and that tests serve as always-current documentation.

Q3. What is Gherkin?

Answer: Gherkin is a structured plain-text language with keywords (Feature, Scenario, Given, When, Then, And, But) used to describe test scenarios in a business-readable format. Cucumber parses Gherkin and executes matching step definitions.

Q4. What are the main components of Cucumber framework?

Answer: Feature files (Gherkin scenarios), step definitions (Java glue code), runner class (@CucumberOptions entry point), hooks (@Before/@After), and dependency injection (PicoContainer) for state sharing.

Q5. Can Cucumber be used without Selenium?

Answer: Yes. Cucumber is a BDD test runner, not a browser automation tool. Step definitions can call REST APIs (RestAssured), database queries, unit test assertions, or any Java code. Selenium is commonly used for UI steps but is not required.

Q6. What is the role of a feature file?

Answer: A feature file describes a feature's behavior through scenarios written in Gherkin. It serves as both an executable test specification and living documentation that business stakeholders can read and approve.

Q7. What is glue code in Cucumber?

Answer: Glue code refers to step definition classes that connect Gherkin steps to executable Java methods. The glue attribute in @CucumberOptions specifies the package(s) containing these classes.

Q8. Is BDD suitable for all projects?

Answer: No. BDD adds value when business stakeholders actively participate and acceptance tests need to be readable. For API-only backends, performance testing, or QA-only teams, traditional TestNG/JUnit frameworks are more efficient.

Q9. What is living documentation?

Answer: Living documentation is test specifications that stay synchronized with the application. When behavior changes, feature files are updated alongside code. Unlike static Word documents, living docs are always accurate because they must pass to be considered valid.

Q10. How does Cucumber integrate with TestNG?

Answer: Create a runner class extending AbstractTestNGCucumberTests with @CucumberOptions. TestNG treats each scenario as a test method. Override the scenarios() DataProvider for parallel execution.

Q11. What is the difference between Cucumber and SpecFlow?

Answer: Cucumber is the original BDD framework supporting Java, JS, Ruby, Python. SpecFlow is the .NET port providing identical Gherkin syntax for C# projects. Both follow the same BDD principles and Gherkin specification.

Q12. What are hooks in Cucumber?

Answer: Hooks are methods annotated with @Before, @After, @BeforeStep, @AfterStep that run at defined points in the scenario lifecycle. They handle setup, teardown, screenshots, and can be conditional using tag expressions like @Before("@ui").

Section 17: BDD Framework Lifecycle

BDD Lifecycle Overview

The BDD lifecycle transforms business requirements into executable, automated tests through a structured collaboration process. Each phase produces artifacts that feed the next, ensuring alignment before a single line of production code is written.

┌──────────────┐    ┌──────────────┐    ┌──────────────┐    ┌──────────────┐
│ Requirement  │───▶│  User Story  │───▶│ Feature File │───▶│   Scenario   │
│  (Epic/Story)│    │  + AC        │    │  (.feature)  │    │  (Gherkin)   │
└──────────────┘    └──────────────┘    └──────────────┘    └──────┬───────┘
                                                                   │
                    ┌──────────────┐    ┌──────────────┐           │
                    │    Report    │◀───│  Execution   │◀──────────┤
                    │  (HTML/Allure│    │  (TestNG/CI) │           │
                    └──────────────┘    └──────────────┘           │
                                                          ┌────────▼───────┐
                                                          │ Step Definition│
                                                          │  (Java glue)   │
                                                          └────────────────┘

Lifecycle Phases Explained

PhaseInputOutputOwner
RequirementBusiness need, stakeholder requestEpic, high-level feature descriptionProduct Owner
User StoryEpic broken into deliverable unitsStory with acceptance criteria in JiraPO + Team
Feature FileAcceptance criteria from user story.feature file with scenarios in GherkinThree Amigos
ScenarioSpecific behavior to validateGiven/When/Then steps in feature fileQA + PO
Step DefinitionGherkin steps from scenariosJava methods with @Given/@When/@ThenSDET / Developer
ExecutionRunner + step definitions + app under testPass/fail results per scenarioCI/CD Pipeline
ReportExecution resultsHTML/Allure/JSON reports for stakeholdersAutomated

Complete BDD Workflow Diagram

                    BDD FRAMEWORK LIFECYCLE
                    ═══════════════════════

    ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
    │                    DISCOVERY PHASE                        │
    │  ┌─────────┐   ┌─────────┐   ┌─────────┐               │
    │  │   PO    │ + │   Dev   │ + │   QA    │  = Three Amigos│
    │  └────┬────┘   └────┬────┘   └────┬────┘               │
    │       └──────────────┼──────────────┘                   │
    │                      ▼                                  │
    │            Discuss examples & edge cases                │
    │            Identify ambiguous requirements                │
    └──────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────┘
                           ▼
    ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
    │                  FORMULATION PHASE                        │
    │       Write Gherkin scenarios with concrete examples      │
    │       Define Given/When/Then for each acceptance criterion│
    │       Add tags (@smoke, @JIRA-1234) for traceability      │
    └──────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────┘
                           ▼
    ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
    │                 AUTOMATION PHASE                          │
    │       Implement step definitions in Java                  │
    │       Wire Selenium/API/DB code behind Gherkin steps       │
    │       Create runner, hooks, DI context                    │
    │       dryRun=true → verify all steps have definitions     │
    └──────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────┘
                           ▼
    ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
    │                  EXECUTION PHASE                          │
    │       Local: mvn test -Dcucumber.filter.tags="@smoke"     │
    │       CI: Jenkins pipeline on every PR merge              │
    │       Parallel: TestNG DataProvider for speed             │
    └──────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────┘
                           ▼
    ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
    │                   REPORTING PHASE                         │
    │       HTML report → QA review                             │
    │       Allure → stakeholder dashboard                      │
    │       Failed scenarios → Jira bug tickets                 │
    └──────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────┘
                           ▼
              Living Documentation (always current)

Three Amigos Meeting

The Three Amigos is a structured collaboration session involving three perspectives before development begins:

RoleContributionQuestions They Ask
Product Owner (PO)Business rules, priorities, acceptance criteria"What should happen when the user enters an expired coupon?"
Developer (Dev)Technical feasibility, edge cases, implementation approach"Can we validate the coupon against an external API or only our DB?"
QA / SDETTest scenarios, negative cases, data requirements"What happens with special characters in the coupon code field?"
Outcome: A shared understanding documented as Gherkin scenarios that all three roles agree represent the intended behavior. No surprises during sprint review.

Discovery → Formulation → Automation Pattern

1. Discovery

  • Explore the user story through conversation and concrete examples.
  • Ask "What if?" questions to uncover edge cases and business rules.
  • Do NOT write Gherkin yet — focus on understanding.
  • Output: agreed examples on a whiteboard or Example Mapping cards.

2. Formulation

  • Convert discovered examples into formal Gherkin scenarios.
  • One scenario = one behavior. Keep scenarios independent.
  • Use Scenario Outline when multiple data combinations test the same behavior.
  • Review with PO for sign-off before automation begins.

3. Automation

  • Implement step definitions mapping to Gherkin steps.
  • Run with dryRun = true first to verify step coverage.
  • Integrate with CI pipeline and tag appropriately.
  • Refactor step definitions for reusability — avoid duplication.

Living Documentation Concept

Living documentation means your test specifications ARE your documentation. Feature files describe what the system does in business language, and they must pass to be valid — so they can never drift out of date.

  • Traditional docs: Written once, outdated within weeks, nobody reads them.
  • Living docs: Updated with every behavior change, executable, always accurate.
  • Published reports: Cucumber HTML reports and Allure dashboards serve as browsable documentation for stakeholders.
  • Cucumber Reports (cloud): Upload JSON results to reports.cucumber.io for team-wide visibility.

How BDD Fits into Agile Sprints

  Sprint N                          Sprint N+1
  ────────                          ──────────

  Day 1-2: Three Amigos             Day 1: Review failed scenarios
           Example Mapping                   from previous sprint
           Write feature files

  Day 2-3: PO sign-off on           Day 2-5: Automate new stories
           Gherkin scenarios                 Refactor step definitions
           Add to repo

  Day 3-5: Implement step           Day 5: Sprint demo using
           definitions                      passing scenarios as
           dryRun → execute                 acceptance evidence
           Fix failures

  Day 5: Demo scenarios             Continuous: CI runs @regression
         as acceptance proof                 on every merge
Sprint ActivityBDD ArtifactCeremony
Sprint PlanningUser stories with acceptance criteriaPlanning poker, story pointing
Early SprintDraft feature files from storiesThree Amigos session
Mid SprintStep definitions + first executionDaily standup — blockers on undefined steps
Sprint ReviewPassing scenarios demo'd to PODemo = living proof of acceptance
Sprint RetroReview flaky scenarios, step duplicationProcess improvement for BDD workflow

BDD Anti-Patterns (What NOT to Do)

  • QA-only BDD — Only QA writes feature files without PO/Dev involvement. Defeats the collaboration purpose.
  • Technical Gherkin — Writing Given I click element #login-btn instead of Given the user is on the login page.
  • Scenario bloat — One scenario with 20 steps testing multiple behaviors. Split into independent scenarios.
  • Imperative steps — When I enter "john" in field 1 and "pass" in field 2 and click submit — too UI-specific.
  • Duplicate step definitions — Multiple Java methods matching the same Gherkin pattern causing ambiguous step errors.
  • Skipping dryRun — Running full execution before verifying all steps have definitions wastes CI time.
  • Feature file as test script — Treating Gherkin like a manual test case with every click documented.
  • No tag strategy — Running all scenarios every time instead of using @smoke, @regression tags.
  • Static test data in features — Hardcoding production-like data instead of using fixtures or factories in step definitions.
  • Ignoring failures — Tagging broken scenarios as @skip permanently instead of fixing or removing them.

Interview Q&A — BDD Framework Lifecycle

Q1. What are the phases of the BDD lifecycle?

Answer: Requirement → User Story → Feature File → Scenario → Step Definition → Execution → Report. Before automation, teams go through Discovery (understand behavior), Formulation (write Gherkin), and Automation (implement step definitions).

Q2. What is a Three Amigos meeting?

Answer: A collaboration session with Product Owner, Developer, and QA/Tester to discuss a user story, explore examples, identify edge cases, and agree on acceptance criteria before writing feature files or code.

Q3. What is Example Mapping?

Answer: A structured technique using colored cards (rules, examples, questions, assumptions) during Three Amigos sessions to break down stories into concrete examples that become Gherkin scenarios.

Q4. Explain Discovery, Formulation, Automation.

Answer: Discovery is conversational exploration of behavior with examples. Formulation converts examples into Gherkin scenarios. Automation implements step definitions and integrates with CI. Each phase has clear entry/exit criteria.

Q5. How does BDD fit in Agile?

Answer: Feature files are created early in the sprint from user stories. Scenarios serve as acceptance criteria, definition of done, and demo evidence. CI runs tagged suites on every commit for continuous validation.

Q6. What is living documentation?

Answer: Executable specifications that stay current with the application. Feature files must pass to be valid, so they cannot become outdated like traditional documentation. Reports provide browsable behavior catalogs.

Q7. What are common BDD anti-patterns?

Answer: QA-only feature writing, UI-specific Gherkin, bloated scenarios, duplicate step definitions, no tag strategy, and treating feature files as manual test scripts instead of behavior descriptions.

Q8. Who should write feature files?

Answer: Ideally the whole Three Amigos team collaboratively. PO provides business rules, QA provides test perspective, Dev confirms feasibility. In practice, QA/SDET often drafts them but PO must review and approve.

Q9. When should you NOT use BDD?

Answer: When there is no business stakeholder involvement, for unit-level testing, performance/load testing, or when the team lacks Gherkin discipline and feature files become unmaintainable UI scripts.

Q10. How do you handle changing requirements in BDD?

Answer: Update the feature file first during Three Amigos review, then update step definitions. The feature file change serves as the specification change request. Version control tracks all modifications.

Section 18: Gherkin Language

Gherkin is the structured plain-text language used by Cucumber to describe software behavior. It uses a defined set of keywords to create readable, executable specifications.

Gherkin Keywords Reference

Feature

Syntax: Feature: <short description> — High-level description of functionality being tested. One Feature keyword per .feature file.

Usage Rules:

  • First keyword in every feature file (after optional comments/tags).
  • Followed by an optional multi-line description explaining business value.
  • Groups related scenarios under one functional area.
Feature: User Login
  As a registered user
  I want to log in to my account
  So that I can access personalized content

  Scenario: Successful login with valid credentials
    ...

Background

Syntax: Background: followed by Given/When/Then steps — Common preconditions executed before every scenario in the feature.

Usage Rules:

  • Runs before EACH scenario in the feature (not once per feature).
  • Use for shared setup like navigating to a page or logging in.
  • Keep minimal — heavy setup slows every scenario.
  • Only one Background per feature file.
Background:
  Given the user is on the login page
  And the login service is available

Scenario

Syntax: Scenario: <description> — A specific test case with Given/When/Then steps.

Usage Rules:

  • One scenario = one behavior/outcome.
  • Scenarios must be independent — no execution order dependency.
  • Use descriptive names: "Successful login with valid credentials" not "Test 1".
Scenario: Reject login with invalid password
  Given the user is on the login page
  When the user enters username "john@example.com"
  And the user enters password "wrongpassword"
  And the user clicks the login button
  Then an error message "Invalid credentials" is displayed

Scenario Outline

Syntax: Scenario Outline: with <placeholder> variables and an Examples: table.

Usage Rules:

  • Template for data-driven scenarios — same steps, different data.
  • Placeholders in angle brackets: <username>, <password>.
  • Cucumber runs one scenario per row in the Examples table.
Scenario Outline: Login with various credentials
  Given the user is on the login page
  When the user enters username "<username>"
  And the user enters password "<password>"
  And the user clicks the login button
  Then the user should see "<expected_result>"

  Examples:
    | username          | password    | expected_result      |
    | john@example.com  | Pass@123    | Welcome dashboard    |
    | invalid@test.com  | wrong       | Invalid credentials  |

Examples

Syntax: Examples: followed by a data table with column headers matching Scenario Outline placeholders.

Usage Rules:

  • Must follow a Scenario Outline (not a regular Scenario).
  • Column headers become placeholder values (without angle brackets).
  • Multiple Examples tables allowed in one Scenario Outline (e.g., grouped by browser).
  • First row is always the header row.

Given

Syntax: Given <precondition> — Sets up the initial context/state.

Usage Rules:

  • Describes state, not actions: "the user is logged in" not "the user logs in".
  • First step in most scenarios (after Background).
  • Use business language: "Given a premium subscription exists" not "Given DB row inserted".
Given the user is on the login page
Given the cart contains 3 items
Given the user has a valid authentication token

When

Syntax: When <action> — Describes the action or event being tested.

Usage Rules:

  • Describes a single key action or event.
  • Use active voice: "When the user submits the order".
  • Avoid UI specifics: "When the user searches for 'laptop'" not "When the user clicks #search-btn".
When the user clicks the login button
When the user searches for "wireless headphones"
When the user applies coupon code "SAVE20"

Then

Syntax: Then <expected outcome> — Asserts the expected result.

Usage Rules:

  • Must be verifiable and observable.
  • One primary outcome per scenario (additional assertions use And).
  • Describe what the user/system sees: "Then the order confirmation is displayed".
Then the user should be redirected to the dashboard
Then the error message "Out of stock" is displayed
Then the order total should be "$89.99"

And

Syntax: And <additional step> — Continues the previous step type (Given, When, or Then).

Usage Rules:

  • Inherits the type of the preceding step (Given/When/Then).
  • Improves readability over repeating Given/When/Then.
  • Can appear multiple times in a scenario.
Given the user is on the checkout page
And the cart contains 2 items
And the user is logged in
When the user selects express shipping
And the user clicks "Place Order"
Then the order confirmation is displayed
And the confirmation email is sent

But

Syntax: But <negative additional step> — Negative continuation of the previous step type.

Usage Rules:

  • Same inheritance rule as And, but for negative assertions or exclusions.
  • Used less frequently than And.
  • Common in Then clauses: "But the discount should not be applied".
Then the search results should contain "laptop"
But should not contain "refurbished" items

Data Tables

Syntax: Pipe-delimited tables passed as arguments to steps.

Usage Rules:

  • Used for structured data within a single step (not Scenario Outline).
  • First row can be headers (passed to DataTable.asMaps()).
  • Ideal for form submissions, menu selections, or multi-field validation.
When the user fills in the registration form:
  | Field           | Value              |
  | First Name      | John               |
  | Last Name       | Doe                |
  | Email           | john@example.com   |
  | Password        | SecurePass@123     |
Then the registration should be successful

Doc Strings

Syntax: Triple quotes """ for multi-line text passed to a step.

Usage Rules:

  • Used for long text: JSON payloads, email bodies, SQL queries, API request bodies.
  • Content between """ delimiters is passed as a single String parameter.
  • Can use content type hint: """json for JSON doc strings.
When the user submits the following JSON payload:
  """
  {
    "productId": "SKU-12345",
    "quantity": 2,
    "couponCode": "SAVE10"
  }
  """
Then the API should return status code 200

Tags

Syntax: @tagname on the line before Feature, Scenario, or Scenario Outline.

Usage Rules:

  • Multiple tags per scenario: @smoke @login @JIRA-1234.
  • Feature-level tags inherit to all scenarios in the feature.
  • Used for selective execution, hooks, and traceability.
  • Common: @smoke, @regression, @wip, @skip, @critical.
@smoke @login
Scenario: Successful login with valid credentials
  Given the user is on the login page
  ...

Complete Feature File Examples

Example 1: Login Feature

@login @authentication
Feature: User Login
  As a registered user
  I want to log in to my account
  So that I can access personalized features

  Background:
    Given the login page is accessible
    And the authentication service is running

  @smoke @positive
  Scenario: Successful login with valid credentials
    Given the user is on the login page
    When the user enters username "john@example.com"
    And the user enters password "SecurePass@123"
    And the user clicks the login button
    Then the user should be redirected to the dashboard
    And the welcome message "Hello, John" should be displayed

  @negative
  Scenario: Login fails with invalid password
    Given a registered user exists with email "john@example.com"
    When the user enters username "john@example.com"
    And the user enters password "wrongpassword"
    And the user clicks the login button
    Then an error message "Invalid credentials" should be displayed
    And the user should remain on the login page

  @negative
  Scenario: Login fails with unregistered email
    Given the user is on the login page
    When the user enters username "unknown@test.com"
    And the user enters password "anypassword"
    And the user clicks the login button
    Then an error message "Account not found" should be displayed

  @social-login
  Scenario: Login via Google OAuth
    Given the user is on the login page
    When the user clicks "Sign in with Google"
    And the user authorizes the application in Google
    Then the user should be redirected to the dashboard
    And the account should be linked to Google

Example 2: Search Feature

@search
Feature: Product Search
  As a shopper
  I want to search for products
  So that I can find items to purchase

  Background:
    Given the user is on the homepage
    And the product catalog contains 500 items

  @smoke
  Scenario: Search by keyword returns matching products
    When the user searches for "wireless headphones"
    Then the search results should contain at least 1 product
    And each result should contain "headphones" in the title

  @filters
  Scenario: Search with price filter
    When the user searches for "laptop"
    And the user applies price filter from "$500" to "$1000"
    Then all displayed products should be priced between $500 and $1000

  @negative
  Scenario: Search with no matching results
    When the user searches for "xyznonexistentproduct123"
    Then the message "No results found" should be displayed
    And the user should see suggested popular products

  Scenario: Search with special characters
    When the user searches for "C++ programming book"
    Then the search results should be displayed without errors
    And results should be relevant to the query

Example 3: Shopping Cart Feature

@cart @ecommerce
Feature: Shopping Cart Management
  As a shopper
  I want to manage items in my cart
  So that I can purchase the products I want

  Background:
    Given the user is logged in
    And the cart is empty

  @smoke
  Scenario: Add a product to cart
    Given a product "Wireless Mouse" priced at "$29.99" is in stock
    When the user adds "Wireless Mouse" to the cart
    Then the cart should contain 1 item
    And the cart total should be "$29.99"

  Scenario: Remove a product from cart
    Given the cart contains the following items:
      | Product         | Quantity | Price   |
      | Wireless Mouse  | 1        | $29.99  |
      | USB Cable       | 2        | $9.99   |
    When the user removes "USB Cable" from the cart
    Then the cart should contain 1 item
    And the cart total should be "$29.99"

  Scenario: Update product quantity in cart
    Given the cart contains "Wireless Mouse" with quantity 1
    When the user updates the quantity of "Wireless Mouse" to 3
    Then the cart should show quantity 3 for "Wireless Mouse"
    And the cart total should be "$89.97"

  @negative
  Scenario: Cannot add out-of-stock product
    Given a product "Limited Edition Watch" is out of stock
    When the user attempts to add "Limited Edition Watch" to the cart
    Then an error message "Product is out of stock" should be displayed
    And the cart should remain empty

Gherkin Best Practices (10+ Points)

  • Write in business language — Use domain terms stakeholders understand, not CSS selectors or XPath.
  • One scenario = one behavior — Test a single outcome. Split complex flows into multiple scenarios.
  • Keep scenarios independent — Each scenario must run in isolation without depending on another scenario's state.
  • Avoid UI-specific language — "When the user searches for laptops" not "When the user clicks the search icon and types in #search-input".
  • Use Background sparingly — Only for truly shared preconditions. Heavy Backgrounds slow every scenario.
  • Descriptive scenario names — Names should explain the behavior: "Reject expired coupon at checkout".
  • Limit steps per scenario — Aim for 3–7 steps. More indicates the scenario tests too much.
  • Use Scenario Outline for data variations — Same behavior with different data belongs in Scenario Outline, not duplicate scenarios.
  • Tag consistently — Establish team conventions for @smoke, @regression, @wip and enforce them.
  • Don't test implementation details — Focus on behavior and outcomes, not internal API calls or database states.
  • Review with PO before automation — Feature files are specifications. Get sign-off before writing step definitions.
  • Avoid conjunctive steps — "When the user enters username and password and clicks login" should be three separate steps.
  • Keep feature files focused — One feature file per functional area. Don't combine login and checkout in one file.

Interview Q&A — Gherkin Language

Q1. What are the primary Gherkin keywords?

Answer: Feature, Background, Scenario, Scenario Outline, Examples, Given, When, Then, And, But. Given sets context, When describes action, Then asserts outcome. And/But continue the preceding step type.

Q2. What is the difference between Scenario and Scenario Outline?

Answer: Scenario is a single test case with fixed data. Scenario Outline is a template with placeholders filled by an Examples table, creating multiple scenario executions from one template.

Q3. What is the purpose of Background?

Answer: Background defines steps that run before every scenario in a feature file. It eliminates duplication of common preconditions like navigating to a page or ensuring a service is available.

Q4. How do Data Tables differ from Examples tables?

Answer: Data Tables pass structured data to a single step within a scenario. Examples tables drive Scenario Outline placeholders, creating multiple scenario executions. Data Tables are for one step; Examples are for entire scenarios.

Q5. What are Doc Strings used for?

Answer: Doc Strings (triple quotes) pass multi-line text to a step definition — commonly JSON payloads, XML, email bodies, or long text content that doesn't fit on one line.

Q6. Can you have multiple Background sections?

Answer: No. Only one Background is allowed per feature file. If you need different setups, use separate feature files or handle setup in individual scenario Given steps.

Q7. What happens if a scenario has no Then step?

Answer: Cucumber allows it, but it's a bad practice. Every scenario should have at least one Then step asserting an observable outcome. Scenarios without assertions don't validate behavior.

Q8. How do tags work at the Feature level?

Answer: Tags placed above the Feature keyword are inherited by all scenarios and scenario outlines in that file. Individual scenarios can have additional tags. Feature tags + scenario tags are combined for filtering.

Q9. What is the difference between And and But?

Answer: Both continue the preceding step type (Given/When/Then). And is for additional steps of the same polarity. But is for negative/additional exclusion assertions, typically after Then.

Q10. How many Feature keywords can a .feature file have?

Answer: Exactly one. Each .feature file describes one feature. Multiple features require multiple .feature files.

Q11. Can Gherkin steps be written in languages other than English?

Answer: Yes. Cucumber supports 70+ languages. Use # language: fr as the first line for French keywords (Fonctionnalité, Étant donné, etc.). The step definition annotations remain in English.

Q12. What makes a good Gherkin scenario?

Answer: Independent, focused on one behavior, written in business language, 3–7 steps, descriptive name, clear Given/When/Then structure, and verifiable Then assertion. Reviewed and approved by PO before automation.

Section 19: Feature Files

Feature File Structure

  • Extension: .feature — plain text files parsed by Cucumber.
  • Location: src/test/resources/features/ (Maven standard).
  • Encoding: UTF-8 recommended for international characters.
  • Structure: Tags → Feature → (Background) → Scenarios/Scenario Outlines.
Convention: Mirror your application module structure. E.g., features/login/login.feature, features/checkout/checkout.feature, features/search/search.feature.

Feature File Naming Conventions

ConventionExampleNotes
Lowercase with underscoresuser_login.featureMost common in Java projects
Lowercase with hyphensuser-login.featureAlternative, equally valid
Match feature nameFeature: User Login → user_login.featureOne file per feature
Module prefixapi_user_login.featureWhen mixing API and UI features
Avoid spacesNever User Login.featureBreaks CI on Linux agents

Complete Feature Files

1. Login Feature (5+ Scenarios)

@login @authentication
Feature: User Login
  As a registered user
  I want to log in to my account
  So that I can access personalized content and services

  Background:
    Given the login page is accessible at "/login"
    And the authentication service is available

  @smoke @positive
  Scenario: Successful login with valid credentials
    Given a registered user exists with email "john@example.com" and password "SecurePass@123"
    When the user enters email "john@example.com"
    And the user enters password "SecurePass@123"
    And the user clicks the "Login" button
    Then the user should be redirected to "/dashboard"
    And the welcome message should contain "Hello, John"

  @negative
  Scenario: Login fails with incorrect password
    Given a registered user exists with email "john@example.com"
    When the user enters email "john@example.com"
    And the user enters password "WrongPassword!"
    And the user clicks the "Login" button
    Then an error message "Invalid email or password" should be displayed
    And the user should remain on the login page

  @negative
  Scenario: Login fails with empty credentials
    Given the user is on the login page
    When the user clicks the "Login" button without entering credentials
    Then validation errors should be displayed for email and password fields

  @negative @security
  Scenario: Login blocked for locked account
    Given a user account "locked@example.com" is locked due to 5 failed attempts
    When the user enters email "locked@example.com"
    And the user enters password "AnyPassword@123"
    And the user clicks the "Login" button
    Then an error message "Account locked. Contact support." should be displayed

  @positive
  Scenario: Remember me keeps user logged in
    Given a registered user exists with email "john@example.com"
    When the user enters email "john@example.com"
    And the user enters password "SecurePass@123"
    And the user checks the "Remember me" checkbox
    And the user clicks the "Login" button
    Then the user should be redirected to "/dashboard"
    When the user closes and reopens the browser
    Then the user should still be logged in on "/dashboard"

Feature: E-Commerce Checkout

    Given the cart contains "Wireless Mouse" with quantity 2
    When the guest user proceeds to checkout
    And the guest enters email "guest@example.com"
    And the guest enters shipping details:
      | Field    | Value                          |
      | Name     | Guest User                     |
      | Address  | 456 Oak Ave, Chicago, IL 60601 |
      | Phone    | 555-0123                       |
    And the guest completes payment
    Then the order confirmation should be displayed
    And a confirmation email should be sent to "guest@example.com"

    And a valid coupon "SAVE10" provides 10% discount
