    Given the user is logged in
    And the cart contains "Wireless Mouse" with quantity 1
    When the user proceeds to checkout
    And the user enters a declined credit card
    And the user clicks "Place Order"
    Then an error message "Payment declined" should be displayed
    And the order should not be created

Background Usage: Shared Preconditions

Background steps execute before every scenario in the feature. Use when all scenarios share the same starting context.

When to use Background: Navigation to a page, ensuring a service is up, setting up test data that ALL scenarios need. Do NOT use Background for scenario-specific setup — use Given steps instead.

Data Tables in Feature Files

Passing a List (single column)

When the user selects the following categories:
  | Electronics |
  | Clothing    |
  | Books       |

Passing a Map (two columns — key/value)

When the user fills in the shipping address:
  | Street  | 123 Main St    |
  | City    | New York       |
  | Zip     | 10001          |

DataTable Class in Step Definitions

// List of maps (header row = keys)
@When("the user fills in the registration form:")
public void fillRegistrationForm(DataTable dataTable) {
    List<Map<String, String>> rows = dataTable.asMaps();
    for (Map<String, String> row : rows) {
        page.enterField(row.get("Field"), row.get("Value"));
    }
}

// List of lists (no headers)
@When("the user selects the following categories:")
public void selectCategories(DataTable dataTable) {
    List<String> categories = dataTable.asList();
    categories.forEach(cat -> page.selectCategory(cat));
}

Scenario Independence Principle

Each scenario must be executable in any order without depending on another scenario's side effects.

  • Do: Set up required state in Given steps or Background.
  • Don't: Assume Scenario 2 runs after Scenario 1 created data.
  • Do: Clean up in @After hooks if scenarios modify shared resources.
  • Don't: Use static variables to pass data between scenarios.

Feature File Organization Strategies

StrategyStructureBest ForExample
By FeatureOne file per application featureMost projects, clear mapping to user storieslogin.feature, checkout.feature
By ModuleSubdirectories per application moduleLarge applications with distinct modulesfeatures/admin/users.feature
By User StoryOne file per Jira storyStrict traceability requirementsJIRA-1234_coupon_checkout.feature
By LayerSeparate API and UI featuresProjects testing both API and UIfeatures/api/, features/ui/

Best Practices for Maintainable Feature Files

  • Keep feature files under 300 lines — split large features into sub-features.
  • One Feature keyword per file — never combine unrelated features.
  • Use consistent step phrasing across all feature files in the project.
  • Tag every scenario with at least @smoke or @regression for selective execution.
  • Link to user stories via @JIRA-XXXX tags for traceability.
  • Review feature files in pull requests — treat them as production code.
  • Avoid hardcoded environment-specific data (URLs, credentials) — use config in step definitions.
  • Delete or update scenarios when features are removed — don't leave orphaned tests.

Interview Q&A — Feature Files

Q1. Where should feature files be located in a Maven project?

Answer: src/test/resources/features/ is the standard location. The path is specified in the runner's @CucumberOptions features attribute. Subdirectories organize by module.

Q2. Can one feature file contain multiple Feature keywords?

Answer: No. Each .feature file must have exactly one Feature keyword. Multiple features require multiple files.

Q3. What is the scenario independence principle?

Answer: Each scenario must run independently in any order. Setup belongs in Given steps or Background, not in dependencies on other scenarios' execution or side effects.

Q4. How do you organize feature files in a large project?

Answer: By application feature/module in subdirectories under features/. Tag with @module tags. Separate API and UI features. Link to Jira stories with @JIRA tags for traceability.

Q5. When should you use Background vs Given?

Answer: Background for preconditions shared by ALL scenarios in a feature. Given for scenario-specific setup. If only 2 of 5 scenarios need a precondition, use Given in those scenarios, not Background.

Q6. How do Data Tables work in feature files?

Answer: Pipe-delimited tables passed as DataTable objects to step definitions. Use asMaps() for header-based key-value rows, asLists() for single-column lists, asList() for flat lists.

Q7. What naming convention do you follow for feature files?

Answer: Lowercase with underscores matching the Feature name: "User Login" → user_login.feature. No spaces. Organized in module subdirectories.

Q8. How do you handle test data in feature files?

Answer: Use Scenario Outline Examples for data variations. Data Tables for form data. Avoid hardcoded production data — step definitions should create test data via APIs or factories. Sensitive data goes in config files, not feature files.

Section 20: Step Definitions

What are Step Definitions?

Step definitions are Java methods annotated with Cucumber annotations (@Given, @When, @Then) that map Gherkin steps from feature files to executable code. Each Gherkin step in a scenario must have exactly one matching step definition method.

Glue Code: Step definitions are often called "glue code" because they glue the human-readable Gherkin specifications to the automation framework (Selenium, RestAssured, etc.).

Step Definition Class Structure

package stepdefinitions;

import io.cucumber.java.en.*;
import pages.LoginPage;
import org.testng.Assert;

public class LoginSteps {

    private LoginPage loginPage;
    private TestContext testContext;

    public LoginSteps(TestContext testContext) {
        this.testContext = testContext;
        this.loginPage = testContext.getLoginPage();
    }

    @Given("the user is on the login page")
    public void userIsOnLoginPage() {
        loginPage.navigateTo("/login");
    }

    @When("the user enters email {string}")
    public void userEntersEmail(String email) {
        loginPage.enterEmail(email);
        testContext.setEmail(email);
    }

    @Then("the user should be redirected to {string}")
    public void userShouldBeRedirected(String expectedUrl) {
        Assert.assertTrue(loginPage.getCurrentUrl().contains(expectedUrl));
    }
}

Regex Parameters vs Cucumber Expressions

FeatureCucumber ExpressionsRegex Patterns
Syntax{string}, {int}, {float}, {word}(.*), (\\d+), (\\d+\\.\\d+)
Default sinceCucumber 4+ (recommended)Cucumber 1–3 (legacy, still supported)
ReadabilityHigh — self-documenting parameter typesLow — regex knowledge required
String capture{string} — matches quoted strings"([^"]*)" or (.*)
Integer capture{int} — matches integers(\\d+)
Float capture{float} — matches decimals(\\d+\\.\\d+)
Word capture{word} — matches single word (no spaces)(\\w+)
Optional textthe user(s) — optional 's'the user(s)?
Alternative textclick(s)/tap(s)click(s)?|tap(s)?
Annotation@Given("user has {int} items")@Given("^user has (\\d+) items$")
Custom parameter typesRegister via ParameterTypeCapture groups with custom conversion

Complete Step Definition Examples

1. LoginSteps.java

package stepdefinitions;

import io.cucumber.datatable.DataTable;
import io.cucumber.java.en.*;
import org.testng.Assert;
import pages.LoginPage;
import utils.TestDataFactory;

public class LoginSteps {

    private final LoginPage loginPage;
    private final TestContext context;

    public LoginSteps(TestContext context) {
        this.context = context;
        this.loginPage = context.getLoginPage();
    }

    @Given("the login page is accessible at {string}")
    public void loginPageAccessible(String path) {
        loginPage.navigateTo(path);
        Assert.assertTrue(loginPage.isPageLoaded());
    }

    @Given("the authentication service is available")
    public void authServiceAvailable() {
        Assert.assertTrue(loginPage.isAuthServiceUp());
    }

    @Given("a registered user exists with email {string} and password {string}")
    public void registeredUserExists(String email, String password) {
        TestDataFactory.createUser(email, password);
    }

    @Given("a user account {string} is locked due to {int} failed attempts")
    public void accountIsLocked(String email, int attempts) {
        TestDataFactory.createLockedUser(email, attempts);
    }

    @Given("the user is on the login page")
    public void userOnLoginPage() {
        loginPage.navigateTo("/login");
    }

    @When("the user enters email {string}")
    public void enterEmail(String email) {
        loginPage.enterEmail(email);
    }

    @When("the user enters password {string}")
    public void enterPassword(String password) {
        loginPage.enterPassword(password);
    }

    @When("the user clicks the {string} button")
    public void clickButton(String buttonText) {
        loginPage.clickButton(buttonText);
    }

    @When("the user checks the {string} checkbox")
    public void checkCheckbox(String label) {
        loginPage.checkCheckbox(label);
    }

    @Then("the user should be redirected to {string}")
    public void verifyRedirect(String expectedPath) {
        Assert.assertTrue(loginPage.getCurrentUrl().contains(expectedPath));
    }

    @Then("the welcome message should contain {string}")
    public void verifyWelcomeMessage(String expectedText) {
        Assert.assertTrue(loginPage.getWelcomeMessage().contains(expectedText));
    }

    @Then("an error message {string} should be displayed")
    public void verifyErrorMessage(String expectedError) {
        Assert.assertEquals(loginPage.getErrorMessage(), expectedError);
    }

    @Then("the user should remain on the login page")
    public void verifyOnLoginPage() {
        Assert.assertTrue(loginPage.getCurrentUrl().contains("/login"));
    }
}

2. SearchSteps.java

package stepdefinitions;

import io.cucumber.java.en.*;
import org.testng.Assert;
import pages.SearchPage;
import java.util.List;

public class SearchSteps {

    private final SearchPage searchPage;
    private List<String> searchResults;

    public SearchSteps(TestContext context) {
        this.searchPage = context.getSearchPage();
    }

    @Given("the user is on the homepage")
    public void userOnHomepage() {
        searchPage.navigateTo("/");
    }

    @Given("the product catalog contains {int} items")
    public void catalogContainsItems(int count) {
        Assert.assertTrue(searchPage.getCatalogCount() >= count);
    }

    @When("the user searches for {string}")
    public void userSearches(String keyword) {
        searchPage.enterSearchTerm(keyword);
        searchPage.clickSearchButton();
        searchResults = searchPage.getResultTitles();
    }

    @When("the user applies price filter from {string} to {string}")
    public void applyPriceFilter(String min, String max) {
        searchPage.setPriceRange(min, max);
        searchResults = searchPage.getResultTitles();
    }

    @Then("the search results should contain at least {int} product")
    public void verifyMinResults(int minCount) {
        Assert.assertTrue(searchResults.size() >= minCount);
    }

    @Then("each result should contain {string} in the title")
    public void verifyResultsContainKeyword(String keyword) {
        searchResults.forEach(title ->
            Assert.assertTrue(title.toLowerCase().contains(keyword.toLowerCase()))
        );
    }

    @Then("the message {string} should be displayed")
    public void verifyMessage(String expectedMessage) {
        Assert.assertEquals(searchPage.getNoResultsMessage(), expectedMessage);
    }

    @Then("all displayed products should be priced between ${int} and ${int}")
    public void verifyPriceRange(int min, int max) {
        searchPage.getResultPrices().forEach(price -> {
            Assert.assertTrue(price >= min && price <= max);
        });
    }
}

3. CheckoutSteps.java

package stepdefinitions;

import io.cucumber.datatable.DataTable;
import io.cucumber.java.en.*;
import org.testng.Assert;
import pages.CheckoutPage;
import pages.CartPage;
import java.util.List;
import java.util.Map;

public class CheckoutSteps {

    private final CheckoutPage checkoutPage;
    private final CartPage cartPage;
    private final TestContext context;

    public CheckoutSteps(TestContext context) {
        this.context = context;
        this.checkoutPage = context.getCheckoutPage();
        this.cartPage = context.getCartPage();
    }

    @Given("the cart contains {string} with quantity {int}")
    public void cartContainsProduct(String product, int qty) {
        cartPage.addProduct(product, qty);
    }

    @Given("a valid coupon {string} provides {int}% discount")
    public void validCouponExists(String code, int percent) {
        context.setCouponCode(code);
        context.setDiscountPercent(percent);
    }

    @When("the user proceeds to checkout")
    public void proceedToCheckout() {
        cartPage.clickCheckout();
    }

    @When("the user applies coupon code {string}")
    public void applyCoupon(String code) {
        checkoutPage.enterCouponCode(code);
        checkoutPage.clickApplyCoupon();
    }

    @When("the user selects payment method {string}")
    public void selectPayment(String method) {
        checkoutPage.selectPaymentMethod(method);
    }

    @When("the user clicks {string}")
    public void clickPlaceOrder(String button) {
        checkoutPage.clickButton(button);
    }

    @When("the guest enters shipping details:")
    public void enterShippingDetails(DataTable dataTable) {
        Map<String, String> details = dataTable.asMap(String.class, String.class);
        checkoutPage.fillShippingForm(details);
    }

    @Then("the order confirmation should be displayed")
    public void verifyOrderConfirmation() {
        Assert.assertTrue(checkoutPage.isConfirmationDisplayed());
    }

    @Then("the order total should be {string}")
    public void verifyOrderTotal(String expectedTotal) {
        Assert.assertEquals(checkoutPage.getOrderTotal(), expectedTotal);
    }

    @Then("the discount of {string} should be applied")
    public void verifyDiscount(String expectedDiscount) {
        Assert.assertEquals(checkoutPage.getDiscountAmount(), expectedDiscount);
    }
}

Parameterized Steps

Cucumber Expressions capture parameters directly from Gherkin text and pass them as method arguments:

// Feature: When the user enters email "john@example.com"
@When("the user enters email {string}")
public void enterEmail(String email) { ... }

// Feature: Then the cart should contain 3 items
@Then("the cart should contain {int} items")
public void verifyCartCount(int count) { ... }

// Feature: When the user waits 5 seconds
@When("the user waits {int} seconds")
public void waitSeconds(int seconds) throws InterruptedException {
    Thread.sleep(seconds * 1000L);
}

Data Table Handling in Step Definitions

import io.cucumber.datatable.DataTable;
import java.util.List;
import java.util.Map;

public class RegistrationSteps {

    // Header row becomes map keys
    @When("the user fills in the registration form:")
    public void fillForm(DataTable dataTable) {
        List<Map<String, String>> rows = dataTable.asMaps();
        for (Map<String, String> row : rows) {
            String field = row.get("Field");
            String value = row.get("Value");
            registrationPage.enterField(field, value);
        }
    }

    // Two-column table as single map
    @When("the user enters shipping address:")
    public void enterAddress(DataTable dataTable) {
        Map<String, String> address = dataTable.asMap(String.class, String.class);
        checkoutPage.fillAddress(
            address.get("Street"),
            address.get("City"),
            address.get("Zip")
        );
    }

    // Single column as list
    @When("the user selects the following categories:")
    public void selectCategories(DataTable dataTable) {
        List<String> categories = dataTable.asList();
        categories.forEach(cat -> filterPage.selectCategory(cat));
    }

    // Raw rows without header treatment
    @Given("the following products are in stock:")
    public void productsInStock(DataTable dataTable) {
        List<List<String>> rows = dataTable.asLists();
        rows.remove(0); // skip header
        rows.forEach(row -> inventoryService.ensureStock(
            row.get(0), row.get(1), Integer.parseInt(row.get(3))
        ));
    }
}

Sharing State Between Steps

Approach 1: PicoContainer Dependency Injection

Add cucumber-picocontainer dependency. Register shared classes in the glue package. Cucumber creates one instance per scenario.

// TestContext.java — shared state container
package stepdefinitions;

public class TestContext {
    private String email;
    private String couponCode;
    private int discountPercent;
    private LoginPage loginPage;
    private CartPage cartPage;

    public TestContext() {
        this.loginPage = new LoginPage();
        this.cartPage = new CartPage();
    }

    public String getEmail() { return email; }
    public void setEmail(String email) { this.email = email; }
    public LoginPage getLoginPage() { return loginPage; }
    public CartPage getCartPage() { return cartPage; }
    // ... other getters/setters
}

// LoginSteps.java — receives TestContext via constructor injection
public class LoginSteps {
    private final TestContext context;

    public LoginSteps(TestContext context) {
        this.context = context;
    }

    @When("the user enters email {string}")
    public void enterEmail(String email) {
        context.getLoginPage().enterEmail(email);
        context.setEmail(email);  // shared with other step classes
    }
}

// CheckoutSteps.java — same TestContext instance injected
public class CheckoutSteps {
    private final TestContext context;

    public CheckoutSteps(TestContext context) {
        this.context = context;
    }

    @Then("a confirmation email should be sent to the user's email")
    public void verifyConfirmationEmail() {
        String email = context.getEmail(); // set by LoginSteps
        Assert.assertTrue(emailService.wasSentTo(email));
    }
}

Approach 2: Scenario Context Pattern

public class ScenarioContext {
    private final Map<String, Object> data = new HashMap<>();

    public void set(String key, Object value) { data.put(key, value); }
    public <T> T get(String key) { return (T) data.get(key); }
    public boolean contains(String key) { return data.containsKey(key); }
}

Step Definition Best Practices

  • Reuse steps — Write generic steps like the user clicks the {string} button instead of one step per button.
  • Keep step definitions thin — Delegate to Page Objects or service classes; don't put Selenium code directly in steps.
  • One responsibility — Each step definition method should do one thing.
  • Consistent phrasing — Agree on step wording across the team and document in a step catalog.
  • Use DI for state — PicoContainer or ScenarioContext, never static variables.
  • Avoid assertions in When steps — When steps perform actions; Then steps perform assertions.
  • Parameter types over regex — Prefer Cucumber Expressions for readability.

Common Errors

ErrorCauseFix
Undefined stepNo matching step definition for a Gherkin stepImplement the missing step or run with dryRun=true to find all undefined steps
Duplicate step definitionTwo methods match the same Gherkin patternRemove or rename the duplicate; check across all glue packages
Ambiguous stepMultiple methods match with overlapping patternsMake patterns more specific; e.g., use {string} instead of (.*)
Pending stepStep definition throws PendingExceptionImplement the step or remove the scenario from execution with @wip tag
Parameter mismatchMethod parameter count/types don't match captured groupsVerify Cucumber Expression parameter types match Gherkin data

Interview Q&A — Step Definitions

Q1. What are step definitions?

Answer: Java methods annotated with @Given, @When, @Then that map Gherkin steps to executable code. They form the glue between feature files and the automation framework.

Q2. What is glue code?

Answer: Another name for step definitions. The glue package (specified in @CucumberOptions) contains all step definition and hook classes that Cucumber scans for matching step patterns.

Q3. Cucumber Expressions vs Regex — which do you prefer?

Answer: Cucumber Expressions ({string}, {int}, {word}) since Cucumber 4. They are readable, self-documenting, and less error-prone. Regex is legacy but still supported for complex patterns.

Q4. How do you share data between step definition classes?

Answer: PicoContainer dependency injection — add cucumber-picocontainer, create a TestContext class, inject it via constructor into all step classes. Each scenario gets a fresh instance.

Q5. How do you handle Data Tables in step definitions?

Answer: Accept DataTable as method parameter. Use asMaps() for header-based rows, asMap() for two-column key-value, asList() for single column, asLists() for raw rows.

Q6. What causes "Duplicate step definition" error?

Answer: Two or more methods in glue packages match the same Gherkin step pattern. Cucumber cannot determine which to invoke. Remove or differentiate the conflicting patterns.

Q7. What is dryRun in Cucumber?

Answer: When dryRun=true, Cucumber verifies all Gherkin steps have matching step definitions without executing them. Useful for validating coverage before full test runs.

Q8. Should step definitions contain Selenium code?

Answer: No. Step definitions should be thin — delegate to Page Object Model classes or service layers. This keeps steps maintainable and reusable across UI changes.

Q9. How do you handle optional parameters in steps?

Answer: Cucumber Expressions support optional text: the user(s) matches "the user" or "the users". For complex optionality, create separate step definitions.

Q10. Can one step definition match multiple Gherkin steps?

Answer: Yes, using alternative text in Cucumber Expressions: @When("the user clicks/taps the {string} button"). Or use multiple annotations on the same method.

Q11. What happens if a step definition throws an exception?

Answer: The scenario fails immediately. Cucumber reports the failing step, exception message, and stack trace in the test report. Subsequent steps in the scenario are skipped.

Q12. How do you organize step definition classes?

Answer: One class per feature domain: LoginSteps, SearchSteps, CheckoutSteps. All in the glue package. Shared utilities in TestContext or helper classes, not duplicated across step classes.

Section 21: Cucumber Runner File

What is a Runner?

The Runner class is the entry point for Cucumber test execution. It tells Cucumber where to find feature files, which packages contain step definitions, which tags to filter, and what report formats to generate. Without a runner, Cucumber doesn't know what to execute.

TestNG Runner vs JUnit Runner

CriteriaTestNG RunnerJUnit Runner
Base ClassAbstractTestNGCucumberTests@RunWith(Cucumber.class) or JUnit Platform
Dependencycucumber-testngcucumber-junit or cucumber-junit-platform-engine
Parallel ExecutionOverride scenarios() DataProvider with parallel=trueJUnit 5 parallel config or surefire parallel settings
Test GroupsTestNG groups integration via tagsJUnit tags (@Tag) with cucumber filter
ReportingTestNG HTML + Cucumber pluginsJUnit reports + Cucumber plugins
CI Integrationmvn test with TestNG suite XMLmvn test with JUnit runner
Industry UsageMore common in Selenium/TestNG projectsCommon in Spring Boot and modern Java projects

@CucumberOptions Annotation Attributes

AttributePurposeExample
featuresPath to feature files or directories"src/test/resources/features"
gluePackages containing step definitions and hooks{"stepdefinitions", "hooks"}
tagsTag expression for selective execution"@smoke and not @skip"
pluginReport format and output location{"pretty", "html:target/cucumber-reports"}
monochromeSimplified console output (no ANSI colors)true
dryRunVerify step definitions without executingtrue
strictFail on undefined or pending steps (deprecated in v7)true
stepNotificationsEmit events for each step (CI integration)true
publishPublish results to Cucumber Reports cloudtrue
snippetsUndefined step snippet formatCucumberOptions.SnippetType.CAMELCASE

Plugin Options

PluginOutputUsage
prettyColored console outputDevelopment and debugging
html:target/cucumber-reportsHTML reportStakeholder review, CI artifacts
json:target/cucumber.jsonJSON reportInput for Allure, custom dashboards
junit:target/cucumber-junit.xmlJUnit XMLJenkins, Azure DevOps test result parsing
io.qameta.allure.cucumber7jvm.AllureCucumber7JvmAllure reportRich reporting with screenshots and history
timeline:target/timelineTimeline HTML reportParallel execution analysis

Complete TestNG Runner Class

package runners;

import io.cucumber.testng.AbstractTestNGCucumberTests;
import io.cucumber.testng.CucumberOptions;
import org.testng.annotations.DataProvider;

@CucumberOptions(
    features = "src/test/resources/features",
    glue = {"stepdefinitions", "hooks"},
    tags = "@smoke and not @skip",
    plugin = {
        "pretty",
        "html:target/cucumber-reports/cucumber.html",
        "json:target/cucumber-reports/cucumber.json",
        "junit:target/cucumber-reports/cucumber-junit.xml",
        "io.qameta.allure.cucumber7jvm.AllureCucumber7Jvm"
    },
    monochrome = true,
    publish = false
)
public class TestRunner extends AbstractTestNGCucumberTests {

    @Override
    @DataProvider(parallel = true)
    public Object[][] scenarios() {
        return super.scenarios();
    }
}

Multiple Runner Files for Different Suites

// SmokeTestRunner.java — fast feedback on every commit
@CucumberOptions(
    features = "src/test/resources/features",
    glue = {"stepdefinitions", "hooks"},
    tags = "@smoke and not @skip",
    plugin = {"pretty", "html:target/smoke-report"}
)
public class SmokeTestRunner extends AbstractTestNGCucumberTests { }

// RegressionTestRunner.java — full suite nightly
@CucumberOptions(
    features = "src/test/resources/features",
    glue = {"stepdefinitions", "hooks"},
    tags = "@regression and not @skip and not @wip",
    plugin = {"pretty", "html:target/regression-report", "json:target/regression.json"}
)
public class RegressionTestRunner extends AbstractTestNGCucumberTests {
    @Override
    @DataProvider(parallel = true)
    public Object[][] scenarios() { return super.scenarios(); }
}

// LoginTestRunner.java — feature-specific runner
@CucumberOptions(
    features = "src/test/resources/features/login",
    glue = {"stepdefinitions", "hooks"},
    tags = "@login",
    plugin = {"pretty", "html:target/login-report"}
)
public class LoginTestRunner extends AbstractTestNGCucumberTests { }

Running from Command Line

# Run all tests via default runner
mvn test

# Run with specific tag filter (overrides runner tags)
mvn test -Dcucumber.filter.tags="@smoke"

# Run smoke excluding skip and wip
mvn test -Dcucumber.filter.tags="@smoke and not @skip and not @wip"

# Run specific runner class
mvn test -Dtest=SmokeTestRunner

# Run with parallel threads
mvn test -Dtest=RegressionTestRunner -Dsurefire.parallel=methods -Dsurefire.threadCount=4

# Dry run to verify step definitions
mvn test -Dtest=TestRunner -Dcucumber.execution.dry-run=true

Tag Expressions: AND, OR, NOT Logic

ExpressionMeaningScenarios Executed
@smokeScenarios tagged @smokeOnly @smoke scenarios
@smoke and @loginBoth tags requiredScenarios with BOTH @smoke AND @login
@smoke or @criticalEither tagScenarios with @smoke OR @critical (or both)
not @skipExclusionAll scenarios EXCEPT those tagged @skip
@regression and not @brokenComplex filterRegression scenarios excluding broken ones
(@smoke or @sanity) and not @wipGrouped logicSmoke or sanity, excluding work-in-progress
@api and @JIRA-1234Traceability filterAPI tests for specific Jira ticket
Precedence: not has highest precedence, then and, then or. Use parentheses for explicit grouping: (@smoke or @sanity) and not @skip.

TestNG Suite XML Integration

<!DOCTYPE suite SYSTEM "https://testng.org/testng-1.0.dtd">
<suite name="Cucumber BDD Suite" parallel="methods" thread-count="4">
    <test name="Smoke Tests">
        <classes>
            <class name="runners.SmokeTestRunner"/>
        </classes>
    </test>
    <test name="Regression Tests">
        <classes>
            <class name="runners.RegressionTestRunner"/>
        </classes>
    </test>
</suite>

Interview Q&A — Cucumber Runner

Q1. What is the purpose of the Cucumber runner class?

Answer: Entry point that configures Cucumber execution — feature file paths, glue packages, tag filters, report plugins, and integration with TestNG/JUnit test engines.

Q2. How do you run Cucumber tests in parallel with TestNG?

Answer: Override the scenarios() method with @DataProvider(parallel = true) in a class extending AbstractTestNGCucumberTests. Configure thread count in TestNG suite XML or Maven surefire plugin.

Q3. What does dryRun=true do?

Answer: Cucumber parses feature files and verifies every Gherkin step has a matching step definition without executing any test code. Reports undefined and ambiguous steps.

Q4. How do you override tags at runtime?

Answer: Pass -Dcucumber.filter.tags="@smoke" on the Maven command line. Runtime tag filter overrides the tags attribute in @CucumberOptions.

Q5. What plugins do you use for reporting?

Answer: pretty for console, html for stakeholder reports, json for Allure/custom dashboards, junit for CI parsing. Allure plugin (io.qameta.allure.cucumber7jvm.AllureCucumber7Jvm) for rich reports with screenshots.

Q6. Can you have multiple runner classes?

Answer: Yes. Common pattern: SmokeTestRunner, RegressionTestRunner, and feature-specific runners. Each with different tags and plugin outputs. Run selectively via -Dtest=ClassName.

Q7. What is the glue attribute?

Answer: Specifies package(s) where Cucumber scans for step definitions and hooks. Multiple packages as array: glue = {"stepdefinitions", "hooks", "utils"}.

Q8. How do you integrate Cucumber with Jenkins?

Answer: Maven command with tag filter parameter, publish HTML report as Jenkins artifact, parse JUnit XML for test results trend, optionally use Cucumber Reports plugin for cucumber.json.

Q9. What is monochrome=true?

Answer: Disables ANSI color codes in console output. Useful for CI environments that don't render colors properly, producing cleaner log files.

Q10. What happens when strict mode finds undefined steps?

Answer: In Cucumber 6 and earlier, strict=true caused build failure on undefined/pending steps. In Cucumber 7+, undefined steps always fail by default; strict is deprecated.

Q11. How do you run only failed scenarios?

Answer: Cucumber doesn't natively support rerun of failures. Workarounds: use @rerun tag manually, third-party plugins, or TestNG retry analyzer on the runner class.

Q12. What is the difference between features path as file vs directory?

Answer: Directory path runs all .feature files recursively. File path runs only that file. Use directory for full suite, file path for focused testing during development.

Section 22: Scenario Outline & Data-Driven BDD

What is Scenario Outline?

A Scenario Outline is a template for data-driven scenarios. Instead of writing separate scenarios for each data combination, you write one template with placeholders and provide data in an Examples table. Cucumber executes one scenario per row in the Examples table.

Key Concept: Scenario Outline = Scenario + Examples table. The outline defines steps with <placeholder> variables. The Examples table provides values for each execution.

Syntax: Scenario Outline + Examples Table

Scenario Outline: <title with placeholders>
  Given ...
  When ... "<placeholder>" ...
  Then ... "<expected>" ...

  Examples:
    | placeholder | expected |
    | value1      | result1  |
    | value2      | result2  |

Complete Examples

1. Login with Multiple Credentials

@login @data-driven
Scenario Outline: Login attempt with various credentials
  Given the user is on the login page
  When the user enters email "<email>"
  And the user enters password "<password>"
  And the user clicks the "Login" button
  Then the user should see "<expected_result>"
  And the page URL should contain "<expected_url>"

  Examples: Valid and invalid credentials
    | email              | password       | expected_result       | expected_url |
    | john@example.com   | SecurePass@123 | Welcome dashboard     | /dashboard   |
    | wrong@test.com     | anypassword    | Invalid credentials   | /login       |
    | john@example.com   | wrongpass      | Invalid credentials   | /login       |
    |                    | SecurePass@123 | Email is required     | /login       |

  Examples: Locked and expired accounts
    | email              | password       | expected_result              | expected_url |
    | locked@example.com | AnyPass@123    | Account locked               | /login       |
    | expired@example.com| OldPass@123    | Password expired             | /reset       |

2. Registration with Various Data Combinations

@registration @data-driven
Scenario Outline: Registration form validation
  Given the user is on the registration page
  When the user enters first name "<first_name>"
  And the user enters email "<email>"
  And the user enters password "<password>"
  And the user enters confirm password "<confirm_password>"
  And the user clicks "Register"
  Then the registration result should be "<result>"
  And the message should contain "<message>"

  Examples:
    | first_name | email              | password       | confirm_password | result  | message                    |
    | John       | john@test.com      | SecurePass@123 | SecurePass@123   | success | Verification email sent    |
    | J          | john@test.com      | SecurePass@123 | SecurePass@123   | failure | Name must be 2+ characters |
    | John       | invalid-email      | SecurePass@123 | SecurePass@123   | failure | Valid email required       |
    | John       | john@test.com      | short          | short            | failure | Password min 8 characters  |
    | John       | john@test.com      | SecurePass@123 | DifferentPass    | failure | Passwords do not match     |

3. Search with Different Keywords and Expected Results

@search @data-driven
Scenario Outline: Product search returns expected results
  Given the product catalog is loaded
  When the user searches for "<keyword>"
  Then the result count should be <min_results>
  And the top result should contain "<expected_in_title>"

  Examples:
    | keyword              | min_results | expected_in_title    |
    | laptop               | 5           | laptop               |
    | wireless mouse       | 3           | mouse                |
    | USB-C cable          | 1           | USB                  |
    | xyznonexistent999    | 0           | No results           |

4. Price Calculation with Quantities and Discounts

@checkout @pricing @data-driven
Scenario Outline: Order total calculation with discounts
  Given the product "<product>" is priced at $<unit_price>
  And a coupon "<coupon>" provides <discount_pct>% discount
  When the user adds <quantity> items to the cart
  And the user applies coupon "<coupon>"
  Then the subtotal should be $<subtotal>
  And the discount should be $<discount>
  And the order total should be $<total>

  Examples:
    | product  | unit_price | quantity | coupon  | discount_pct | subtotal | discount | total  |
    | Widget   | 50         | 2        | SAVE10  | 10           | 100.00   | 10.00    | 90.00  |
    | Widget   | 50         | 1        | NONE    | 0            | 50.00    | 0.00     | 50.00  |
    | Gadget   | 200        | 3        | SAVE20  | 20           | 600.00   | 120.00   | 480.00 |
    | Gadget   | 200        | 5        | BULK15  | 15           | 1000.00  | 150.00   | 850.00 |

Examples Table: Column Headers as Placeholders

Column headers in the Examples table (without angle brackets) map directly to placeholders in the Scenario Outline (with angle brackets):

Scenario Outline: Placeholder mapping
  When the user enters "<username>"     ← placeholder
  Then the result is "<expected>"       ← placeholder

  Examples:
    | username | expected  |            ← column headers = placeholder names
    | john     | success   |
    | jane     | success   |

Multiple Examples Tables in One Scenario Outline

Scenario Outline: Cross-browser login verification
  Given the user opens the app in <browser>
  When the user logs in with valid credentials
  Then the dashboard should load within <timeout> seconds

  @chrome
  Examples: Chrome browser
    | browser | timeout |
    | chrome  | 5       |
    | chrome  | 3       |

  @firefox
  Examples: Firefox browser
    | browser | timeout |
    | firefox | 8       |
    | firefox | 5       |

  @edge
  Examples: Edge browser
    | browser | timeout |
    | edge    | 6       |

Scenario Outline vs Data Tables Comparison

CriteriaScenario Outline + ExamplesData Tables in Steps
ScopeEntire scenario executed per rowData passed to a single step
Placeholders<name> in any step in the outlineTable rows passed as DataTable parameter
Report granularityEach row = separate scenario in reportsOne scenario regardless of table size
Use caseSame behavior, different input/output pairsStructured data for one action (form fill, list selection)
Step definitionStandard parameters from placeholdersDataTable parameter with asMaps()/asList()
Multiple tablesMultiple Examples sections per outlineMultiple Data Tables in different steps
ReadabilityHigh for business — data visible in feature fileHigh for complex form data within a step

When to Use Scenario Outline vs DataProvider

Use Scenario Outline WhenUse TestNG DataProvider When
Data is business-meaningful and PO should review itData is technical (API payloads, binary inputs)
Same Gherkin steps apply to all data rowsTest logic varies significantly per data set
Living documentation needs to show data examplesLarge datasets (100+ rows) from Excel/CSV/DB
Small to medium datasets (< 50 rows)Performance-critical execution needing fine control
BDD workflow with Three Amigos reviewNon-BDD TestNG tests without Gherkin layer

Performance Considerations with Many Examples

  • Each Examples row = one full scenario execution — 100 rows means 100 browser startups if not optimized.
  • Use Background wisely — heavy Background steps multiply across all rows.
  • Tag subsets — Run full Examples only in regression; use @smoke with fewer rows for CI.
  • Parallel execution — TestNG parallel DataProvider runs outline rows concurrently.
  • Large datasets — For 100+ combinations, consider TestNG DataProvider reading from CSV instead of inline Examples.
  • Session reuse — Use @Before hooks to reuse browser sessions where safe, reducing startup overhead.

Interview Q&A — Scenario Outline & Data-Driven BDD

Q1. What is Scenario Outline?

Answer: A parameterized scenario template with placeholders (<name>) filled by an Examples table. Cucumber runs one scenario execution per row, enabling data-driven BDD testing.

Q2. How do placeholders work?

Answer: Placeholders in angle brackets in the Scenario Outline match column headers in the Examples table. Each row provides values substituted into all steps before execution.

Q3. Can a Scenario Outline have multiple Examples tables?

Answer: Yes. Each named Examples section adds rows. Useful for grouping data by browser, environment, or test category. All rows execute as separate scenarios.

Q4. Scenario Outline vs Data Tables — when to use which?

Answer: Scenario Outline when the entire scenario repeats with different data (login attempts). Data Tables when structured data is passed to a single step (form fields, product lists).

Q5. How many Examples rows is too many?

Answer: Beyond 50 rows, consider external data sources (CSV, database) with TestNG DataProvider. Inline Examples are best for 5–30 business-meaningful combinations reviewable by PO.

Q6. Do Examples table values support expressions?

Answer: No. Examples values are literal strings substituted into steps. Calculations and dynamic data should happen in step definitions, not in the Examples table.

Q7. How are Scenario Outline rows reported?

Answer: Each row appears as a separate scenario in Cucumber reports: "Login attempt with various credentials — Example #1.1". Failures pinpoint the exact data row.

Q8. Can placeholders appear in Scenario Outline title?

Answer: Yes. Scenario Outline: Login with <email> substitutes the value in reports, making failures easier to identify.

Q9. How do you skip specific Examples rows?

Answer: Tag individual Examples sections (not rows). To skip rows, remove them or comment out. Cucumber doesn't support row-level tags within Examples.

Q10. Scenario Outline with TestNG parallel execution?

Answer: Override scenarios() with @DataProvider(parallel = true). Each Examples row runs as an independent parallel test. Configure thread count in suite XML or surefire plugin.

Q11. What is the difference between Scenario Outline and repeating Scenarios?

Answer: Scenario Outline avoids duplication — one step template, multiple data rows. Separate scenarios duplicate steps, increasing maintenance when steps change. Outline is DRY; separate scenarios are more readable for vastly different flows.

Q12. Can Examples data come from external files?

Answer: Not natively in Gherkin. Examples must be inline in the feature file. For external data, use TestNG DataProvider or custom Cucumber plugins. Some teams generate feature files from CSV in build pipelines.

Section 23: Cucumber Tags

What are Tags?

Tags are labels attached to Feature files and Scenarios that serve as metadata for organizing, filtering, and controlling test execution. Tags enable selective running of test subsets without modifying feature files or step definitions.

Syntax: Tags start with @ and appear on the line immediately before Feature, Scenario, or Scenario Outline. Multiple tags are space-separated: @smoke @login @JIRA-1234.

Tag Syntax

@smoke @login @JIRA-5678
Feature: User Login
  ...

  @negative
  Scenario: Invalid password login
    ...

  @positive @critical
  Scenario: Successful login
    ...

Common Tag Conventions

CategoryTagsPurpose
Test Suite@smoke, @regression, @sanity, @criticalDefine which suite a scenario belongs to
Test Layer@api, @ui, @db, @e2eIndicate the testing layer or technology
Status@wip, @skip, @broken, @manualControl execution status and track work
Traceability@sprint-42, @JIRA-1234, @US-567Link scenarios to sprint, ticket, or user story
Feature Area@login, @checkout, @search, @paymentGroup by functional area
Environment@staging-only, @prod-safe, @localEnvironment-specific execution control
Speed@fast, @slowIdentify scenarios by execution time for CI optimization

Tag Expressions in Runner

ExpressionDescriptionUse Case
tags = "@smoke"Run only @smoke scenariosCI pipeline on every commit
tags = "@smoke and @login"Intersection — both tags requiredSmoke test login functionality only
tags = "@smoke or @critical"Union — either tag matchesPriority tests for pre-release
tags = "not @skip"Exclusion — skip tagged scenariosRun everything except skipped
tags = "@regression and not @broken"Complex — regression minus brokenNightly regression excluding known failures
tags = "(@smoke or @sanity) and not @wip"Grouped with parenthesesQuick validation excluding WIP
tags = "@api and @JIRA-1234"Feature + ticket filterRun tests for specific bug fix

Tag Inheritance

Tags at the Feature level are inherited by all scenarios and scenario outlines within that feature. Scenario-level tags are added to (not replacing) inherited tags.

@regression @checkout          ← Feature-level tags (inherited)
Feature: E-Commerce Checkout

  @smoke                         ← Scenario inherits: @regression @checkout @smoke
  Scenario: Complete purchase
    ...

  @negative @payment             ← Inherits: @regression @checkout @negative @payment
  Scenario: Declined payment
    ...
Filtering: tags = "@smoke and @regression" matches the first scenario above because it inherits @regression from the Feature and has its own @smoke tag.

Jenkins Parameter Integration

# Jenkinsfile — parameterized tag execution
pipeline {
    parameters {
        choice(name: 'TEST_TAGS', choices: ['@smoke', '@regression', '@sanity'], description: 'Tag to run')
    }
    stages {
        stage('Test') {
            steps {
                sh "mvn test -Dcucumber.filter.tags=${params.TEST_TAGS}"
            }
        }
    }
}

# Command line override
mvn test -Dcucumber.filter.tags="@smoke and not @skip"
mvn test -Dcucumber.filter.tags="@regression and @checkout"
mvn test -Dcucumber.filter.tags="not @wip and not @broken"

Tag-Based Hooks

Hooks can be conditional on tags, running only for scenarios matching the tag expression:

public class Hooks {

    @Before("@ui")
    public void setUpBrowser() {
        DriverFactory.initBrowser("chrome");
    }

    @Before("@api")
    public void setUpApiContext() {
        RestAssured.baseURI = Config.getBaseUrl();
    }

    @After("@ui")
    public void tearDownBrowser(Scenario scenario) {
        if (scenario.isFailed()) {
            Screenshots.capture(scenario);
        }
        DriverFactory.quitDriver();
    }

    @Before("@db")
    public void setUpDatabase() {
        DatabaseHelper.resetTestData();
    }

    @Before("@login")
    public void ensureLoginPageReady() {
        // Runs only for scenarios tagged @login
        loginPage.navigateTo("/login");
    }
}

Tag Strategy for a Real Project

TagPurposeWhen AddedWho Uses
@smokeCritical path tests for CI gateDuring Three Amigos — identified as must-passDevOps (CI), QA Lead
@regressionFull regression suite for nightly runsWhen scenario is stable and approvedQA Team, CI (nightly)
@wipWork in progress — not ready for CIDuring development of new scenarioSDET (removed when done)
@skipTemporarily disabled scenarioWhen feature is deprecated or blockedQA Lead (with Jira link)
@brokenKnown failure — bug loggedWhen a bug is found but not yet fixedSDET, QA Lead
@JIRA-1234Traceability to specific ticketDuring sprint planning with user storyPO, QA, Dev
@apiAPI-level test (no browser)When scenario tests REST/GraphQL endpointsSDET, Dev
@uiBrowser-based UI testWhen scenario requires Selenium/PlaywrightSDET
@criticalBusiness-critical functionalityPO identifies as revenue/compliance criticalPO, QA Lead
@sprint-42Sprint-specific new testsSprint planning for new featuresScrum Team

Tag Best Practices

  • Define a tag catalog — Document all approved tags and their meanings in the project wiki or README.
  • Every scenario gets a suite tag — At minimum @smoke or @regression on every scenario.
  • Don't over-tag — 2–4 tags per scenario is sufficient. Too many tags make filtering confusing.
  • Remove @wip promptly — WIP tags left after completion cause scenarios to be excluded from CI.
  • @broken requires a Jira ticket — Never tag as broken without a linked defect.
  • Consistent naming — lowercase, hyphen-separated: @user-login not @UserLogin or @user_login.
  • Feature tags for broad filtering — @checkout on Feature level avoids tagging every scenario individually.

Interview Q&A — Cucumber Tags

Q1. What are Cucumber tags?

Answer: Metadata labels (@tagname) attached to features and scenarios for organizing, filtering, and controlling test execution. They enable selective running of test subsets via tag expressions in the runner or command line.

Q2. How does tag inheritance work?

Answer: Tags on a Feature are inherited by all scenarios within that feature. Scenario-level tags are additive. A scenario tagged @smoke in a Feature tagged @regression effectively has both tags.

Q3. Explain tag expression operators.

Answer: AND (intersection — both tags required), OR (union — either tag), NOT (exclusion). Precedence: not > and > or. Parentheses for grouping: (@smoke or @sanity) and not @skip.

Q4. How do you run specific tags from the command line?

Answer: mvn test -Dcucumber.filter.tags="@smoke and not @skip". This overrides the tags attribute in @CucumberOptions at runtime.

Q5. What is the difference between @skip and @wip?

Answer: @wip marks scenarios under active development — not yet ready. @skip marks stable scenarios temporarily disabled (deprecated feature, blocked dependency). Both exclude from default CI runs via not @skip and not @wip filters.

Q6. How do tag-based hooks work?

Answer: @Before("@ui") runs before scenarios tagged @ui. @After("@api") runs after API scenarios. Enables conditional setup/teardown without affecting all scenarios.

Q7. Can you tag individual rows in Examples tables?

Answer: No. Tags apply to Feature, Scenario, or Scenario Outline level. Individual Examples sections can be named but not tagged separately. To skip rows, remove them from the table.

Q8. How do you design a tag strategy for CI/CD?

Answer: @smoke on every commit (5–15 min), @regression nightly (full suite), @critical before release, not @skip and not @wip and not @broken on all CI runs. Jenkins parameterized with tag choice for on-demand runs.

Q9. What tags do you use for traceability?

Answer: @JIRA-XXXX linking to tickets, @sprint-XX for sprint tracking, @US-XXX for user story IDs. Enables filtering tests by requirement and verifying coverage per story.

Q10. How many tags should a scenario have?

Answer: 2–4 tags typically: one suite tag (@smoke/@regression), one feature tag (@login), one traceability tag (@JIRA-XXX), optionally one layer tag (@ui/@api). More tags create filtering complexity without added value.

Section 24: Cucumber Hooks

What Are Hooks?

Hooks in Cucumber are blocks of code that run at specific points in the test lifecycle — before or after scenarios and steps. They provide setup and teardown logic that keeps feature files clean and centralizes cross-cutting concerns like browser initialization, database seeding, logging, and screenshot capture.

Key Idea: Hooks decouple infrastructure concerns from business-readable Gherkin. Scenarios describe what to test; hooks handle how the environment is prepared and cleaned up.

Hook Annotations Overview

AnnotationScopeWhen It Runs
@BeforeScenarioBefore each scenario (after background steps)
@AfterScenarioAfter each scenario completes (pass or fail)
@BeforeStepStepBefore each step definition executes
@AfterStepStepAfter each step definition executes
@BeforeAllSuiteOnce before all scenarios (Cucumber 7+)
@AfterAllSuiteOnce after all scenarios (Cucumber 7+)

@Before — Runs Before Each Scenario

Use @Before to launch browsers, reset application state, create test data, or start logging for every scenario.

@Before
public void setUp() {
    driver = DriverFactory.getDriver();
    driver.manage().window().maximize();
    logger.info("Scenario setup complete");
}

@After — Runs After Each Scenario

Use @After for cleanup: quit browser, delete temp files, rollback DB transactions, or capture evidence on failure.

@After
public void tearDown(Scenario scenario) {
    if (scenario.isFailed()) {
        captureScreenshot(scenario);
    }
    DriverFactory.quitDriver();
}

@BeforeStep and @AfterStep

Step-level hooks run around every Gherkin step. Useful for fine-grained logging, highlighting elements before interaction, or capturing screenshots on step failure.

@BeforeStep
public void beforeStep(Scenario scenario) {
    logger.info("Starting step in scenario: " + scenario.getName());
}

@AfterStep
public void afterStep(Scenario scenario) {
    if (scenario.isFailed()) {
        byte[] screenshot = ((TakesScreenshot) driver)
            .getScreenshotAs(OutputType.BYTES);
        scenario.attach(screenshot, "image/png", "Step Failure");
    }
}

Hook with Scenario Parameter

Passing the Scenario object gives access to scenario metadata at runtime:

  • Name: scenario.getName()
  • Status: scenario.isFailed(), scenario.getStatus()
  • Tags: scenario.getSourceTagNames()
  • URI: scenario.getUri() — feature file path
  • Line: scenario.getLine() — scenario line number
@After
public void logScenarioResult(Scenario scenario) {
    logger.info("Scenario: " + scenario.getName()
        + " | Status: " + scenario.getStatus()
        + " | Tags: " + scenario.getSourceTagNames());
}

Conditional Hooks with Tags

Tag expressions in hook annotations restrict execution to matching scenarios. This avoids unnecessary setup for unrelated tests.

@Before("@login or @checkout")
public void setUpAuthContext() {
    // Only runs for login or checkout scenarios
    authToken = AuthService.getTestToken();
}

@Before("@database")
public void setUpDatabase() {
    dbHelper.connect();
    dbHelper.seedTestData();
}

@After("@database")
public void tearDownDatabase() {
    dbHelper.truncateTables();
    dbHelper.disconnect();
}

Hook Execution Order

When multiple hooks of the same type exist, use the order attribute (lower numbers run first for @Before; higher numbers run first for @After).

@Before(order = 0)
public void connectDatabase() { dbHelper.connect(); }

@Before(order = 1)
public void launchBrowser() { driver = DriverFactory.getDriver(); }

@Before(order = 2)
public void navigateToBaseUrl() { driver.get(ConfigReader.get("base.url")); }

@After(order = 2)
public void captureScreenshotOnFailure(Scenario scenario) { /* ... */ }

@After(order = 1)
public void quitBrowser() { DriverFactory.quitDriver(); }

@After(order = 0)
public void disconnectDatabase() { dbHelper.disconnect(); }
Order Rule: @Before hooks run ascending (0 → 1 → 2). @After hooks run descending (2 → 1 → 0) — mirroring a stack: last setup in, first teardown out.

Complete Hooks Class

package hooks;

import io.cucumber.java.*;
import org.openqa.selenium.*;
import org.slf4j.Logger;
import org.slf4j.LoggerFactory;
import utils.DriverFactory;
import utils.ConfigReader;
import utils.DatabaseHelper;

public class Hooks {

    private static final Logger logger = LoggerFactory.getLogger(Hooks.class);
    private WebDriver driver;
    private DatabaseHelper dbHelper;

    // ── One-time suite setup (Cucumber 7+) ──
    @BeforeAll
    public static void beforeAll() {
        logger.info("=== Test Suite Started ===");
        ConfigReader.load("qa");
    }

    @AfterAll
    public static void afterAll() {
        logger.info("=== Test Suite Finished ===");
    }

    // ── Scenario-level setup ──
    @Before(order = 0)
    public void startLogging(Scenario scenario) {
        logger.info("▶ Starting scenario: {} | Tags: {}",
            scenario.getName(), scenario.getSourceTagNames());
    }

    @Before(order = 1)
    public void launchBrowser() {
        driver = DriverFactory.getDriver();
        driver.manage().window().maximize();
        driver.get(ConfigReader.get("base.url"));
    }

    @Before(value = "@database", order = 0)
    public void setUpDatabase() {
        dbHelper = new DatabaseHelper();
        dbHelper.connect();
        dbHelper.insertTestUser("testuser", "pass123");
    }

    // ── Step-level hooks ──
    @BeforeStep
    public void logStep(Scenario scenario) {
        logger.debug("Executing step in: {}", scenario.getName());
    }

    @AfterStep
    public void screenshotOnStepFailure(Scenario scenario) {
        if (scenario.isFailed()) {
            attachScreenshot(scenario, "Step Failure Screenshot");
        }
    }

    // ── Scenario-level teardown ──
    @After(order = 2)
    public void captureFailureScreenshot(Scenario scenario) {
        if (scenario.isFailed()) {
            attachScreenshot(scenario, "Scenario Failure Screenshot");
            logger.error("✘ Scenario FAILED: {}", scenario.getName());
        } else {
            logger.info("✔ Scenario PASSED: {}", scenario.getName());
        }
    }

    @After(order = 1)
    public void quitBrowser() {
        DriverFactory.quitDriver();
    }

    @After(value = "@database", order = 0)
    public void cleanUpDatabase() {
        dbHelper.deleteTestUser("testuser");
        dbHelper.disconnect();
    }

    private void attachScreenshot(Scenario scenario, String name) {
        try {
            byte[] screenshot = ((TakesScreenshot) driver)
                .getScreenshotAs(OutputType.BYTES);
            scenario.attach(screenshot, "image/png", name);
        } catch (Exception e) {
            logger.warn("Could not capture screenshot: {}", e.getMessage());
        }
    }
}

@BeforeAll / @AfterAll (Cucumber 7+)

Suite-level hooks run once per test run — ideal for loading configuration, initializing report directories, or warming up connection pools. Methods must be static.

@BeforeAll
public static void globalSetup() {
    Files.createDirectories(Paths.get("target/screenshots"));
    RestAssured.baseURI = ConfigReader.get("api.base.url");
}

@AfterAll
public static void globalTeardown() {
    EmailNotifier.sendSummaryReport();
}

Hooks vs TestNG @BeforeMethod Comparison

AspectCucumber HooksTestNG @BeforeMethod
ScopeScenario / Step / SuiteTest method (Java method annotated with @Test)
Tag filteringBuilt-in via tag expressions (@Before("@smoke"))Via groups (@BeforeMethod(groups="smoke"))
Scenario contextScenario parameter with name, tags, statusITestResult or Method parameter
Step-level control@BeforeStep / @AfterStepNot available natively
Execution orderorder attribute on annotationdependsOnMethods, priority
IntegrationWorks standalone or with TestNG runnerNative TestNG lifecycle
Screenshot attachscenario.attach() embeds in Cucumber reportsManual — listener or Reporter.log()

Hook Best Practices

  • Keep hooks thin — delegate heavy logic to utility classes; hooks should orchestrate, not implement.
  • Use tag-based conditional hooks — avoid running DB setup for UI-only scenarios.
  • Always set hook order explicitly when multiple hooks exist — implicit order is fragile.
  • Capture screenshots in @After, not @Before — browser state reflects the failure point.
  • Use @BeforeAll/@AfterAll sparingly — static state can cause issues in parallel runs.
  • Never put assertions in hooks — hooks prepare/teardown; steps validate behavior.
  • Make hooks idempotent — safe to run even if a prior step partially succeeded.
  • Log scenario name and tags — essential for debugging parallel and tagged runs.

Interview Q&A — Cucumber Hooks

#QuestionAnswer
1What are Cucumber hooks?Java methods annotated with @Before, @After, @BeforeStep, @AfterStep that run setup/teardown at scenario or step boundaries.
2When does @Before run relative to Background?@Before runs after Background steps but before the scenario's own steps.
3How do you run a hook only for @login scenarios?@Before("@login") — Cucumber evaluates the tag expression against scenario tags.
4What is the order attribute?Controls execution sequence; lower order runs first for @Before, reverse for @After.
5How do you attach a screenshot to a report?scenario.attach(bytes, "image/png", "name") in an @After or @AfterStep hook.
6Can hooks access the Scenario object?Yes — inject Scenario as a method parameter in @Before, @After, @BeforeStep, @AfterStep.
7Difference between @Before and @BeforeAll?@Before runs before each scenario; @BeforeAll runs once before the entire test suite (static method, Cucumber 7+).
8Can you have multiple @Before hooks?Yes — use order attribute to control sequence; all matching hooks execute.
9What happens if a @Before hook throws an exception?The scenario is marked failed/skipped; subsequent steps do not run; @After hooks still execute.
10Hooks vs Background in feature file?Background is Gherkin-level shared steps visible in reports; hooks are invisible Java infrastructure code.
11How to skip browser launch for @api tagged scenarios?Do not put browser launch in global @Before; use @Before("not @api") or a dedicated @Before("@ui") hook.
12Are hooks thread-safe in parallel execution?Each scenario gets its own hook instance in parallel mode if using ThreadLocal for driver/state.

Section 25: Cucumber Reporting

Built-in Cucumber Report Plugins

Cucumber generates reports via plugins configured in the runner class. Each plugin produces a different output format for console, CI, or third-party dashboards.

PluginOutputUse Case
prettyColored console outputLocal development, quick feedback
html:pathHTML report fileShareable static report in target folder
json:pathJSON fileInput for Extent, Allure, Jenkins Cucumber plugin
junit:pathJUnit XMLCI tools expecting JUnit format (Jenkins, Azure)
timeline:pathTimeline HTMLVisualize parallel scenario execution timing
message:pathNDJSON messagesCucumber Reports Service, custom parsers

Multiple Plugins in Runner

@CucumberOptions(
    features = "src/test/resources/features",
    glue = {"stepdefinitions", "hooks"},
    plugin = {
        "pretty",
        "html:target/cucumber-report.html",
        "json:target/cucumber.json",
        "junit:target/cucumber-junit.xml",
        "timeline:target/timeline/index.html"
    },
    tags = "@smoke",
    monochrome = true
)
public class TestRunner extends AbstractTestNGCucumberTests { }

Cucumber Built-in HTML Report

The HTML plugin generates a self-contained report showing features, scenarios, steps, pass/fail status, duration, and error stack traces. Open target/cucumber-report.html in a browser after test execution.

  • Feature summary — pass/fail counts per feature file
  • Scenario drill-down — step-by-step results with timing
  • Error details — stack traces for failed steps
  • Tags display — shows which tags were executed

Extent Reports with Cucumber

Extent Reports provides rich, dashboard-style HTML reports with charts, system info, and screenshot embedding.

Dependencies (pom.xml)

<dependency>
    <groupId>tech.grasshopper</groupId>
    <artifactId>extentreports-cucumber7-adapter</artifactId>
    <version>1.14.0</version>
</dependency>

Runner Configuration

plugin = {
    "pretty",
    "json:target/cucumber.json",
    "com.aventstack.extentreports.cucumber.adapter.ExtentCucumberAdapter:"
}

spark-config.xml Customization

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<extentreports>
    <configuration>
        <theme>STANDARD</theme>
        <documentTitle>BDD Automation Report</documentTitle>
        <reportName>QA Regression Results</reportName>
        <timeStampFormat>MMM dd, yyyy HH:mm:ss</timeStampFormat>
        <encoding>UTF-8</encoding>
        <protocol>HTTPS</protocol>
    </configuration>
</extentreports>

Place spark-config.xml in src/test/resources. Extent auto-discovers it.

Complete Extent Setup

// Hooks.java — embed screenshot in Extent via Scenario.attach
@After
public void attachScreenshot(Scenario scenario) {
    if (scenario.isFailed()) {
        byte[] screenshot = ((TakesScreenshot) driver)
            .getScreenshotAs(OutputType.BYTES);
        scenario.attach(screenshot, "image/png", "Failure Screenshot");
    }
}

// extent.reporter.spark.out=target/SparkReport/Spark.html
// extent.reporter.spark.config=src/test/resources/spark-config.xml

Allure Reports with Cucumber

Dependency

<dependency>
    <groupId>io.qameta.allure</groupId>
    <artifactId>allure-cucumber7-jvm</artifactId>
    <version>2.25.0</version>
</dependency>

plugin = {
    "pretty",
    "io.qameta.allure.cucumber7jvm.AllureCucumber7Jvm"
}

Allure Annotations in Step Definitions

import io.qameta.allure.*;

@Step("Login with username: {0}")
public void login(String username, String password) {
    loginPage.enterUsername(username);
    loginPage.enterPassword(password);
    loginPage.clickLogin();
}

@Attachment(value = "Screenshot", type = "image/png")
public byte[] captureScreenshot() {
    return ((TakesScreenshot) driver).getScreenshotAs(OutputType.BYTES);
}

@Description("Verify user can login with valid credentials")
@Given("I am logged in as {string}")
public void iAmLoggedInAs(String user) {
    login(user, "password123");
}

Generate Allure Report

mvn clean test
allure serve target/allure-results

Cucumber Reports Service (Online)

reports.cucumber.io is Cucumber's cloud reporting platform. Publish results by setting environment variables:

export CUCUMBER_PUBLISH_ENABLED=true
mvn clean test

Alternatively, use the message plugin output and upload via CI pipeline. Provides team dashboards, trend analysis, and shareable links without hosting reports locally.

Screenshot Embedding in Reports

The Scenario.attach() method embeds bytes into Cucumber-compatible reports (HTML, Allure, Extent).

@After
public void embedEvidence(Scenario scenario) {
    if (scenario.isFailed()) {
        // Screenshot
        byte[] screenshot = ((TakesScreenshot) driver)
            .getScreenshotAs(OutputType.BYTES);
        scenario.attach(screenshot, "image/png", "Failure Screenshot");

        // Page source on failure
        String pageSource = driver.getPageSource();
        scenario.attach(pageSource, "text/html", "Page Source");

        // Log snippet
        scenario.attach("Current URL: " + driver.getCurrentUrl(),
            "text/plain", "Debug Info");
    }
}

@AfterStep
public void embedStepScreenshot(Scenario scenario) {
    if (scenario.isFailed()) {
        byte[] screenshot = ((TakesScreenshot) driver)
            .getScreenshotAs(OutputType.BYTES);
        scenario.attach(screenshot, "image/png",
            "Failed Step: " + scenario.getName());
    }
}

1How do you generate an HTML report in Cucumber?Add "html:target/report.html" to the plugin array in @CucumberOptions.
2What is the purpose of the JSON plugin?Produces machine-readable output consumed by Extent, Allure, Jenkins Cucumber Reports plugin.

4How to integrate Allure with Cucumber 7?Add allure-cucumber7-jvm dependency and AllureCucumber7Jvm plugin; run allure serve after tests.
5What is ExtentCucumberAdapter?A plugin that converts Cucumber events into Extent Reports Spark dashboard format.

12How to customize Extent report title and theme?Configure spark-config.xml with documentTitle, reportName, and theme elements.

Section 26: TestNG + Cucumber Integration

Why Integrate TestNG with Cucumber?

Cucumber excels at the BDD layer — Gherkin features, step definitions, hooks. TestNG excels at the execution layer — parallel runs, grouping, listeners, XML suites, and CI integration. Combining both gives you readable tests with enterprise-grade execution control.

Cucumber ProvidesTestNG Provides
Gherkin feature filesParallel scenario execution
Step definitions & hookstestng.xml suite configuration
Tag-based filteringGroups and listeners
Scenario-level reportingRetry analyzer, ITestListener
Data Tables & Scenario Outline@DataProvider for parallel scenarios

Architecture Overview

┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                     testng.xml                           │
│              (parallel, groups, listeners)               │
└────────────────────────┬─────────────────────────────────┘
                         ▼
┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              TestRunner (extends                         │
│         AbstractTestNGCucumberTests)                     │
│              @CucumberOptions                            │
└────────────────────────┬─────────────────────────────────┘
                         ▼
┌──────────────┐  ┌──────────────┐  ┌──────────────────────┐
│ Feature Files│→ │Step Definitions│→ │ Page Objects / API  │
│  (.feature)  │  │   + Hooks    │  │     Utilities       │
└──────────────┘  └──────────────┘  └──────────────────────┘
                         ▼
              ┌──────────────────────┐
              │  Reports & Listeners │
              │ (Allure, Extent, etc)│
              └──────────────────────┘

AbstractTestNGCucumberTests — Base Runner Class

Extend AbstractTestNGCucumberTests from io.cucumber.testng to bridge Cucumber scenarios as TestNG test methods.

package runners;

import io.cucumber.testng.AbstractTestNGCucumberTests;
import io.cucumber.testng.CucumberOptions;
import org.testng.annotations.DataProvider;

@CucumberOptions(
    features = "src/test/resources/features",
    glue = {"stepdefinitions", "hooks"},
    plugin = {
        "pretty",
        "html:target/cucumber-report.html",
        "json:target/cucumber.json",
        "io.qameta.allure.cucumber7jvm.AllureCucumber7Jvm"
    },
    tags = "@smoke"
)
public class TestRunner extends AbstractTestNGCucumberTests {

    @Override
    @DataProvider(parallel = true)
    public Object[][] scenarios() {
        return super.scenarios();
    }
}

Parallel Scenario Execution

Override the scenarios() data provider with parallel = true. Control thread count via testng.xml.

<suite name="BDD Suite" parallel="methods" thread-count="4">
  <test name="Cucumber Tests">
    <classes>
      <class name="runners.TestRunner"/>
    </classes>
  </test>
</suite>
Thread Safety: Use ThreadLocal for WebDriver and scenario-scoped state when running scenarios in parallel. Never share a single driver instance across threads.

TestNG Listeners with Cucumber

// Custom listener for retry and reporting
public class RetryListener implements IAnnotationTransformer {
    @Override
    public void transform(ITestAnnotation annotation,
                          Class testClass,
                          Constructor testConstructor,
                          Method testMethod) {
        annotation.setRetryAnalyzer(RetryAnalyzer.class);
    }
}

// RetryAnalyzer.java
public class RetryAnalyzer implements IRetryAnalyzer {
    private int count = 0;
    private static final int MAX_RETRY = 2;

    @Override
    public boolean retry(ITestResult result) {
        if (count < MAX_RETRY) {
            count++;
            return true;
        }
        return false;
    }
}
<listeners>
    <listener class-name="listeners.RetryListener"/>
    <listener class-name="listeners.TestReportListener"/>
</listeners>

TestNG Groups with Cucumber Tags Mapping

Map Cucumber tags to TestNG groups for suite-level filtering:

// SmokeRunner.java — tags = "@smoke"
@CucumberOptions(tags = "@smoke", ...)

// RegressionRunner.java — tags = "@regression"
@CucumberOptions(tags = "@regression", ...)
<suite name="Full Regression" parallel="methods" thread-count="4">
  <test name="Smoke">
    <classes><class name="runners.SmokeRunner"/></classes>
  </test>
  <test name="Regression">
    <classes><class name="runners.RegressionRunner"/></classes>
  </test>
</suite>

Execution Flow

Maven/TestNG
     │
     ▼
testng.xml ──→ loads TestRunner class
     │
     ▼
AbstractTestNGCucumberTests
     │
     ├── @BeforeAll hooks (Cucumber)
     ├── For each scenario (parallel via DataProvider):
     │     ├── @Before hooks
     │     ├── Background steps
     │     ├── Scenario steps → Step Definitions
     │     ├── @After hooks (screenshot, cleanup)
     │     └── TestNG ITestListener callbacks
     ├── @AfterAll hooks (Cucumber)
     └── Generate reports (HTML, JSON, Allure)

Interview Q&A — TestNG + Cucumber Integration

#QuestionAnswer
1Why integrate TestNG with Cucumber?TestNG adds parallel execution, XML suites, listeners, retry, and CI-friendly grouping on top of Cucumber's BDD layer.
2What class do you extend for TestNG + Cucumber?AbstractTestNGCucumberTests from io.cucumber.testng package.
3How to run Cucumber scenarios in parallel?Override scenarios() @DataProvider with parallel=true; set thread-count in testng.xml.
4Can TestNG @Test annotations run Cucumber scenarios?No — Cucumber scenarios become TestNG tests via AbstractTestNGCucumberTests, not via @Test.
5How to run only @smoke tagged scenarios?tags = "@smoke" in @CucumberOptions, or -Dcucumber.filter.tags="@smoke" on CLI.
6Do TestNG listeners work with Cucumber?Yes — register ITestListener implementations in testng.xml; they fire for each scenario.
7How to implement retry for flaky scenarios?IRetryAnalyzer + IAnnotationTransformer registered as TestNG listener.
8Can you have multiple Cucumber runners in one suite?Yes — define multiple <test> blocks in testng.xml, each pointing to a different runner class.
9What happens to Cucumber hooks in parallel mode?Each parallel scenario gets its own hook execution; use ThreadLocal for shared resources.
10Cucumber standalone runner vs TestNG runner?Standalone uses @Suite + Cucumber class; TestNG uses AbstractTestNGCucumberTests for TestNG features.
11How to pass parameters from testng.xml to Cucumber?Use system properties (-Denv=qa) read by ConfigReader in hooks or step definitions.
12Does TestNG @BeforeMethod work with Cucumber scenarios?It runs but is not recommended — use Cucumber @Before/@After hooks for scenario lifecycle instead.

Section 27: Selenium + TestNG + Cucumber Full Framework

Framework Architecture

A production-ready BDD automation framework layers Gherkin features on top of Page Object Model, with TestNG driving parallel execution and Cucumber managing scenario lifecycle through hooks.
