Run via IDE (right-click → TestNG), Maven surefire plugin, or testng.xml suite. Example: @Test public void addTest() { Assert.assertEquals(2+2, 4); }. No main method needed; TestNG discovers @Test methods automatically.

Interviewer expects: Working syntax and awareness of multiple execution methods.

Q5: What is testng.xml and why is it used?

Answer: testng.xml is a TestNG suite configuration file written in XML. It defines which tests to run, groups to include/exclude, parallel execution settings, listeners, and parameters. It allows running subsets of tests without recompiling code. QA teams use it to create smoke, regression, and sanity suites. CI/CD pipelines reference testng.xml for consistent test selection across environments.

Interviewer expects: Understanding that XML decouples test selection from code — critical for CI pipelines.

Q6: What is the difference between @BeforeClass and @BeforeMethod?

Answer: @BeforeClass runs once before all test methods in a class; @BeforeMethod runs before each @Test method. Use @BeforeClass for expensive one-time setup like WebDriver initialization in non-parallel runs. Use @BeforeMethod for per-test setup like clearing cookies, navigating to base URL, or resetting test data. In parallel method execution, @BeforeClass is shared across threads — a common pitfall.

Interviewer expects: Practical guidance on when to use each, including parallel execution caveats.

Q7: What is the @Test annotation?

Answer: @Test marks a method as a test case executable by TestNG. Attributes include priority, groups, dependsOnMethods, enabled, timeOut, dataProvider, expectedExceptions, and retryAnalyzer. Without @Test, TestNG ignores the method. Multiple @Test methods can exist in one class. TestNG reports pass/fail/skip status per @Test method in HTML and XML reports.

Interviewer expects: Knowledge of key attributes, not just "it marks a test."

Q8: What assertion methods does TestNG provide?

Answer: TestNG provides assertEquals, assertNotEquals, assertTrue, assertFalse, assertNull, assertNotNull, assertSame, assertNotSame, and fail(). All are static methods in org.testng.Assert. assertEquals handles objects, strings, and primitives with optional message parameter. SoftAssert (org.testng.asserts.SoftAssert) collects multiple failures and reports them via assertAll() — useful for form validation with many fields.

Interviewer expects: Mention SoftAssert as differentiator; know assertEquals vs assertSame distinction.

Q9: What is the difference between hard assert and soft assert?

Answer: Hard assert (Assert.assertEquals) stops test execution immediately on failure. Soft assert (SoftAssert) continues executing subsequent assertions and reports all failures at assertAll(). Use hard assert for critical checkpoints (login succeeded). Use soft assert for non-blocking validations (multiple UI field checks). SoftAssert must be instantiated per test method; never use static SoftAssert in parallel tests.

Interviewer expects: Real-world usage scenario, not just definition.

Q10: What are TestNG groups and how do you use them?

Answer: Groups categorize tests for selective execution. Assign via @Test(groups = {"smoke", "regression"}). In testng.xml, use <include> and <exclude> under <groups><run> to filter. A test can belong to multiple groups. Groups enable smoke runs on every commit and full regression nightly. Maven: mvn test -Dgroups=smoke. Groups differ from Cucumber tags but serve the same filtering purpose.

Interviewer expects: XML syntax fluency and CI integration use case.

Q11: How do you skip a test in TestNG?

Answer: Set @Test(enabled = false) to skip a test programmatically. In testng.xml, exclude groups or specific classes. Use dependsOnMethods — if dependency fails, dependent tests skip automatically. ITestListener.onTestSkipped captures skipped tests in custom reports. Skipped ≠ Failed: skipped tests don't indicate defects. Use skip for known broken features tracked in Jira.

Interviewer expects: Distinguish skip vs fail and know multiple skip mechanisms.

Q12: What is test priority in TestNG?

Answer: @Test(priority = 1) controls execution order within a class. Lower numbers run first. Default priority is 0. Priority only affects methods in the same class — not across classes. Unlike dependsOnMethods, priority doesn't skip tests on failure. Use priority for logical ordering (create before read). Best practice: prefer dependsOnMethods for true dependencies, priority for ordering convenience.

Interviewer expects: Know priority limitations and not confuse with dependsOnMethods.

Q13: What is dependsOnMethods in TestNG?

Answer: @Test(dependsOnMethods = {"loginTest"}) ensures the current test runs only if loginTest passes. If dependency fails, TestNG marks this test as SKIPPED. Can depend on multiple methods: dependsOnMethods = {"a", "b"}. Dependencies work within the same class by default. Cross-class dependencies require dependsOnGroups or careful suite ordering. Overusing dependencies creates brittle test chains — prefer independent tests.

Interviewer expects: Understand skip behavior and warn against over-coupling tests.

Q14: How do you run TestNG tests from command line?

Answer: Via Maven: mvn clean test (uses surefire plugin). Specify suite: mvn test -DsuiteXmlFile=testng.xml. Run single class: mvn test -Dtest=LoginTest. Direct TestNG: java -cp "testng.jar:classes" org.testng.TestNG testng.xml. IDE: right-click class or XML → Run As TestNG Suite. CI: Jenkins executes mvn test with suite parameter per environment.

Interviewer expects: Maven command fluency — most teams use Maven, not raw java -cp.

Q15: What is the @Parameters annotation?

Answer: @Parameters({"browser", "url"}) injects values from testng.xml <parameter> tags into test methods. XML: <parameter name="browser" value="chrome"/>. Method: public void test(@Optional("chrome") String browser). @Optional provides default if parameter missing. Useful for cross-browser testing and environment URLs. Limitation: only supports String parameters — use @DataProvider for complex types.

Interviewer expects: XML-to-method mapping and @Optional awareness.

Q16: What reports does TestNG generate by default?

Answer: TestNG generates index.html (main report), emailable-report.html (concise summary), and testng-results.xml (JUnit-compatible XML). Reports show passed, failed, skipped counts with method-level detail and execution time. Output goes to test-output/ folder by default. Custom reports via IReporter listener or ExtentReports integration. CI tools parse testng-results.xml for trend dashboards.

Interviewer expects: Know default output location and CI integration via XML results.

Q17: What is @BeforeSuite used for?

Answer: @BeforeSuite runs once before any tests in the entire suite — even before @BeforeTest. Use for global setup: load config properties, establish DB connection pool, initialize ExtentReports, set system properties. Must be in a class included in the suite. Pair with @AfterSuite for cleanup (close connections, flush reports). Only one @BeforeSuite executes per suite regardless of class count.

Interviewer expects: Suite-level vs class-level scope distinction with concrete examples.

Q18: What is @BeforeTest vs @BeforeClass?

Answer: @BeforeTest runs once per <test> tag in testng.xml — before any classes in that test block. @BeforeClass runs once per class. A suite with two <test> blocks triggers @BeforeTest twice. Use @BeforeTest for per-suite-section setup (e.g., API base URL for API test block). @BeforeClass is for class-specific setup (Page Object initialization).

Interviewer expects: Map annotations to testng.xml structure — this is a common trick question.

Q19: How do you include/exclude test classes in testng.xml?

Answer: Include specific classes: <classes><class name="com.tests.LoginTest"/></classes>. Include packages: <packages><package name="com.tests.ui"/></packages>. Exclude methods: <class name="LoginTest"><methods><exclude name="brokenTest"/></methods></class>. Combine groups with classes for granular control. Exclude takes precedence over include within the same level.

Interviewer expects: XML fluency including method-level include/exclude.

Q20: What is expectedExceptions in @Test?

Answer: @Test(expectedExceptions = IllegalArgumentException.class) marks test as PASS when the specified exception is thrown. Optional: expectedExceptionsMessageRegExp = "Invalid input". Use to validate error handling code. If exception is NOT thrown, test fails. If wrong exception type thrown, test fails. Don't use for normal flow testing — only for verifying exception paths.

Interviewer expects: Correct use case (negative testing exceptions) not as a workaround for bugs.

Q21: What is the timeOut attribute in @Test?

Answer: @Test(timeOut = 5000) fails the test if execution exceeds 5000 milliseconds. Useful for detecting hung tests, infinite loops, or slow API responses. Applies per invocation — with invocationCount=3, each invocation gets its own timeout. Different from implicit Selenium waits. Combine with retryAnalyzer for flaky timeout failures. Set timeouts based on SLA requirements, not arbitrary values.

Interviewer expects: Distinguish TestNG timeout from Selenium WebDriverWait.

Q22: What is invocationCount in TestNG?

Answer: @Test(invocationCount = 5) runs the test method 5 times. Used for stress testing, flaky test detection, and load simulation. Each invocation is independent — separate @BeforeMethod/@AfterMethod cycles. Report shows each invocation separately. Combine with threadPoolSize for parallel invocations: @Test(invocationCount = 10, threadPoolSize = 5) runs 10 times with 5 threads.

Interviewer expects: Know threadPoolSize pairing and reporting implications.

Q23: How do you pass multiple parameters to a test method?

Answer: Use @DataProvider for complex/multi-type parameters: @Test(dataProvider = "data") with Object[][] return. Use @Parameters for simple string params from XML. DataProvider supports any object type — strings, integers, custom POJOs. DataProvider methods can be in the same class or another class (dataProviderClass attribute). DataProvider is the standard approach for data-driven testing in TestNG.

Interviewer expects: DataProvider as primary approach; @Parameters for simple cases only.

Q24: What is the @Factory annotation?

Answer: @Factory marks a method that returns Object[] of test class instances. TestNG invokes each instance as a separate test class. Use case: run same test class with different browsers/configurations. Example: return new Object[] { new LoginTest("chrome"), new LoginTest("firefox") }. Each instance gets its own @BeforeClass/@AfterClass cycle. Enables data-driven class-level testing unlike @DataProvider which drives methods.

Interviewer expects: Factory vs DataProvider distinction — class-level vs method-level data driving.

Q25: What is the difference between @BeforeGroups and @BeforeClass?

Answer: @BeforeGroups({"smoke"}) runs before the first test method in the "smoke" group across all classes. @BeforeClass runs before all methods in a specific class regardless of groups. @BeforeGroups is group-scoped and cross-class; @BeforeClass is class-scoped. Use @BeforeGroups for group-specific setup like preparing smoke test data. @AfterGroups runs after the last method in the group completes.

Interviewer expects: Cross-class group scope understanding.

Q26: How do you configure TestNG with Maven?

Answer: Add testng dependency and maven-surefire-plugin in pom.xml. Configure suiteXmlFiles: <suiteXmlFiles><suiteXmlFile>testng.xml</suiteXmlFile></suiteXmlFiles>. Set testng version in dependencies. Run mvn clean test. Override via -DsuiteXmlFile or -Dtest on command line. Surefire plugin version 3.x supports TestNG 7.x. Add testng.xml to src/test/resources or project root.

Interviewer expects: Actual pom.xml configuration, not just "add dependency."

Q27: What is assertTrue vs assertEquals?

Answer: assertTrue(condition) verifies a boolean expression is true — use for isDisplayed(), isEnabled(), contains(). assertEquals(actual, expected) compares two values for equality — use for text, numbers, status codes. assertTrue(isLoggedIn) vs assertEquals(welcomeMsg, "Welcome"). assertTrue with complex conditions reduces readability — prefer assertEquals when comparing specific values. Both accept optional failure message.

Interviewer expects: Appropriate usage context, not interchangeable use.

Q28: Can TestNG tests be run without testng.xml?

Answer: Yes. TestNG discovers @Test annotated methods via classpath scanning. Run from IDE by right-clicking a test class. Maven surefire runs all test classes matching *Test, Test*, *Tests, *TestCase patterns by default. testng.xml is optional but recommended for suite control, parallel config, and CI. Without XML, all @Test methods in matched classes execute — no group filtering.

Interviewer expects: Know both paths; recommend XML for real projects.

Q29: What is the @Optional annotation?

Answer: @Optional("defaultValue") on @Parameters provides fallback when testng.xml doesn't supply the parameter. Example: @Parameters({"browser"}) public void test(@Optional("chrome") String browser). Without @Optional, missing parameter causes TestNG to fail at startup. Useful for local development where XML may not specify all parameters. Can combine with @Parameters and @DataProvider in the same class for different methods.

Interviewer expects: Practical default-value pattern for flexible test configuration.

Q30: What happens when a TestNG test fails?

Answer: TestNG marks the method as FAILED in reports, continues executing remaining tests (unless configured otherwise). @AfterMethod still runs after failed tests — use for screenshot capture. Dependent tests (dependsOnMethods) are SKIPPED. Suite continues unless configured with configfailurepolicy. ITestListener.onTestFailure fires for custom handling. CI marks build as unstable/failed based on surefire results.

Interviewer expects: AfterMethod still runs, dependents skip — shows lifecycle mastery.

Intermediate (35)

Q31: What is @DataProvider in TestNG?

Answer: DataProvider supplies data to test methods via @Test(dataProvider="name"). Method returns Object[][] or Iterator. Runs before each matching test invocation. Supports parallel=true for concurrent data iteration. Can live in same class or external class via dataProviderClass.

Interviewer expects: Ability to write a working DataProvider with Object[][] return type.

Q32: How does DataProvider differ from @Parameters?

Answer: @Parameters reads static String values from testng.xml — limited to strings. DataProvider is a Java method returning dynamic data of any type from Excel, DB, or APIs. @Parameters suits environment config; DataProvider suits test data matrices. Both can coexist in the same project.

Interviewer expects: Clear decision criteria for when to use each mechanism.

Q33: Can DataProvider be in a different class?

Answer: Yes. Use @Test(dataProvider="name", dataProviderClass = DataClass.class). The DataProvider method must be static in the external class. Common pattern: TestDataProvider utility class centralizes all test data. Keeps test classes clean and data reusable across multiple test classes.

Interviewer expects: Know dataProviderClass attribute and static method requirement.

Q34: How do you run DataProvider tests in parallel?

Answer: Set @DataProvider(parallel = true) on the provider method. Control threads via suite thread-count or dataproviderthreadcount in testng.xml. Each data row runs as a separate parallel invocation. Ensure thread-safe WebDriver using ThreadLocal and independent test data per thread.

Interviewer expects: ThreadLocal pattern for parallel data-driven UI tests.

Q35: What is parallel execution in TestNG?

Answer: TestNG runs tests concurrently using parallel attribute in testng.xml: tests, classes, methods, or instances. thread-count sets max concurrent threads. Reduces total execution time for large suites. Requires thread-safe code — static shared state causes random failures in parallel mode.

Interviewer expects: XML configuration and thread-safety awareness.

Q36: What are parallel modes in TestNG?

Answer: parallel="tests": each test block runs concurrently. parallel="classes": classes within a test run concurrently. parallel="methods": @Test methods run concurrently. parallel="instances": @Factory instances run concurrently. Choose based on isolation level — methods mode needs most thread safety.

Interviewer expects: Match parallel mode to test isolation capabilities.

Q37: How do you configure thread-count in testng.xml?

Answer: Set thread-count on suite tag: parallel="methods" thread-count="5". Override via -Dthreadcount=10. data-provider-thread-count controls DataProvider parallelism separately. Start with CPU core count and tune based on execution stability and CI agent capacity.

Interviewer expects: Practical tuning approach, not just XML syntax.

Q38: What is a TestNG listener?

Answer: Listeners hook into TestNG lifecycle events via interfaces like ITestListener, ISuiteListener, IInvokedMethodListener. Register via @Listeners annotation, testng.xml listeners tag, or ServiceLoader. Use for screenshots, logging, custom reports, and retry logic. Multiple listeners execute in registration order.

Interviewer expects: Name specific listener interfaces and registration methods.

Q39: What is ITestListener used for?

Answer: ITestListener callbacks: onTestStart, onTestSuccess, onTestFailure, onTestSkipped. Most common listener for automation frameworks. Use onTestFailure to capture screenshots and attach logs. onTestStart logs test name and timestamp. Essential for production-grade automation reporting.

Interviewer expects: Concrete onTestFailure screenshot implementation mention.

Q40: How do you implement a custom TestNG listener?

Answer: Create class implementing ITestListener or extending TestListenerAdapter. Override desired methods. Register via @Listeners on test class or listener class-name in testng.xml for global scope. Keep listener logic lightweight to avoid slowing test execution. Example: screenshot on failure.

Interviewer expects: Working registration approach and real use case.

Q41: What is IRetryAnalyzer?

Answer: IRetryAnalyzer decides whether to re-run a failed test via retry(ITestResult result). Return true to retry, false to stop. Track retry count with instance variable. Assign via @Test(retryAnalyzer = MyRetry.class). Global retry via IAnnotationTransformer. Always cap max retries to prevent infinite loops.

Interviewer expects: Max retry cap and thread-safety for retry counter.

Q42: How do you retry failed tests in TestNG?

Answer: Implement IRetryAnalyzer with max retry count of 1-2. Assign to @Test or globally via IAnnotationTransformer. Alternative: surefire rerunFailingTestsCount=2. Log retry attempts in listener for flaky test tracking. Retry infrastructure failures, not assertion failures that indicate real bugs.

Interviewer expects: Distinguish flaky infrastructure retry vs masking real bugs.

Q43: What is IAnnotationTransformer?

Answer: IAnnotationTransformer modifies @Test annotations at runtime in transform() method. Set retryAnalyzer, groups, or enabled attributes dynamically. Register as listener in testng.xml. Use case: apply RetryAnalyzer to all tests without annotating each method. Read system properties to enable/disable tests per environment.

Interviewer expects: Runtime annotation modification for enterprise framework control.

Q44: What is test dependency in TestNG?

Answer: dependsOnMethods and dependsOnGroups create execution dependencies. Dependent test runs only if dependency passes; otherwise SKIPPED. Use for workflow tests: createUser then loginUser. Anti-pattern: long dependency chains. Prefer self-contained tests with API setup over dependsOnMethods.

Interviewer expects: Balance between workflow testing and test independence.

Q45: What is dependsOnGroups?

Answer: @Test(dependsOnGroups = {"setup"}) runs after all methods in the setup group pass. Cross-class dependency mechanism. If any method in setup group fails, dependent test skips. Combine with @BeforeGroups for group-level setup and teardown across multiple classes.

Interviewer expects: Cross-class dependency pattern knowledge.

Q46: How do you share data between TestNG test methods?

Answer: Instance variables for sequential tests. ThreadLocal for parallel safety. TestNG ITestContext setAttribute/getAttribute for suite-level sharing. @DataProvider for parameterized input. Never share mutable WebDriver without ThreadLocal. For API tests, create data in @BeforeClass and store token in instance field.

Interviewer expects: ThreadLocal as the correct parallel-safe approach.

Q47: What is ITestContext?

Answer: ITestContext provides runtime execution context. Inject via @BeforeMethod setup(ITestContext ctx). Methods: getName(), getAttribute(), setAttribute(), getPassedTests(). Share data: ctx.setAttribute("token", jwt). Scoped to current test tag in XML. Useful for passing auth tokens between methods.

Interviewer expects: Practical attribute sharing across methods in same test block.

Q48: What is XmlSuite and programmatic TestNG execution?

Answer: XmlSuite, XmlTest, XmlClass build suites programmatically without XML files. Create suite in code, set parallel mode, then TestNG testng = new TestNG(); testng.setXmlSuites(list); testng.run(). Useful for dynamic CI pipelines generating suites from git diff or changed files.

Interviewer expects: Advanced skill showing CI/CD integration capability.

Q49: How do you run specific test methods from testng.xml?

Answer: Use methods inside class tag with include name for specific methods or exclude name to skip. More precise than running entire class. Combine with groups for maximum flexibility. Maven: mvn test -Dtest=LoginTest#testValidLogin for single method execution.

Interviewer expects: Method-level XML include/exclude syntax.

Q50: What is the difference between suite, test, and class in TestNG XML?

Answer: Suite is the root execution run. Test is a logical grouping with its own parameters and groups. Class is a Java test class within a test block. One suite can have multiple tests; each test can have multiple classes. parallel=tests parallelizes at test block level.

Interviewer expects: Hierarchy mapping: suite > test > class > method.

Q51: How do you integrate TestNG with Selenium WebDriver?

Answer: Initialize WebDriver in @BeforeMethod with ThreadLocal pattern. Use Page Object Model for interactions. Quit driver in @AfterMethod. Pass driver to Page Objects via constructor. Combine with listeners for screenshot on failure. Cucumber + TestNG + Selenium is the standard BDD stack.

Interviewer expects: ThreadLocal driver pattern mandatory for parallel Selenium.

Q52: What is ThreadLocal WebDriver pattern?

Answer: ThreadLocal stores separate WebDriver per thread. DriverFactory: static ThreadLocal, getDriver creates if null, quitDriver quits and removes. Essential for parallel methods or DataProvider parallel. Without ThreadLocal, threads overwrite driver reference causing random cross-test failures.

Interviewer expects: Explain why static WebDriver fails in parallel.

Q53: How do you handle WebDriver in @BeforeMethod vs @BeforeClass?

Answer: @BeforeClass with single driver works sequentially but breaks in parallel methods mode. @BeforeMethod with ThreadLocal is correct for parallel methods. @BeforeClass with ThreadLocal works for parallel classes mode. Match driver lifecycle to your parallel configuration.

Interviewer expects: Match driver lifecycle to parallel configuration.

Q54: What is TestNG assert log output?

Answer: TestNG reports assertion failures with expected vs actual in HTML report. Custom message: Assert.assertEquals(actual, expected, "Login should succeed"). ITestListener.onTestFailure receives ITestResult with getThrowable(). ExtentReports captures assertion messages with screenshots for richer CI debugging.

Interviewer expects: Custom failure messages for debuggable CI reports.

Q55: How do you disable a test conditionally?

Answer: IAnnotationTransformer reads system property and sets test.setEnabled(false). @Test(enabled=false) for static disable. SkipException in @BeforeMethod marks test SKIPPED dynamically. Check environment in @BeforeMethod — if staging unavailable, skip with logged reason.

Interviewer expects: SkipException for dynamic conditional skipping.

Q56: What is SkipException in TestNG?

Answer: throw new SkipException("reason") marks test as SKIPPED. Unlike failure, skip means test could not run due to environment or missing feature. Reported separately in CI dashboards. Use in @BeforeMethod to skip all methods when precondition fails like API being down.

Interviewer expects: Skip vs Fail distinction with environment example.

Q57: How do you run TestNG tests in Jenkins?

Answer: Pipeline stage: sh 'mvn clean test -DsuiteXmlFile=smoke.xml'. Publish TestNG Results plugin parses testng-results.xml. Archive HTML reports. Parameterize suite and environment. Matrix job for cross-browser. Set unstable vs failed based on team policy.

Interviewer expects: CI pipeline integration with report publishing.

Q58: What is the surefire plugin role with TestNG?

Answer: maven-surefire-plugin executes tests during mvn test phase. Configures suiteXmlFiles, includes/excludes, rerunFailingTestsCount. Reports to target/surefire-reports/. Without surefire, mvn test won't run TestNG. forkCount controls JVM forks for parallel class execution.

Interviewer expects: pom.xml surefire configuration knowledge.

Q59: How do you pass system properties to TestNG tests?

Answer: Command line: mvn test -Dbrowser=firefox -Denv=staging. Read via System.getProperty. Maven resource filtering in testng.xml for parameter values. @BeforeSuite reads properties to configure framework. System properties override config file values for CI parameterization.

Interviewer expects: Property precedence: system > env > config file.

Q60: What is configfailurepolicy in TestNG?

Answer: configfailurepolicy skip or continue on test tag. Controls behavior when @BeforeMethod fails. continue: remaining tests attempt to run. skip: all tests in class skip if config method fails. Set explicitly based on whether partial results are valuable in your pipeline.

Interviewer expects: Configuration failure handling strategy.

Q61: How do you implement test ordering across classes?

Answer: TestNG doesn't guarantee cross-class order. Options: dependsOnGroups, separate test blocks in XML order, or priority within same class only. Best practice: make tests independent. Don't rely on cross-class ordering — it creates fragile suites.

Interviewer expects: Independence over ordering — mature testing perspective.

Q62: What is preserve-order in TestNG XML?

Answer: preserve-order true runs classes and methods in XML declaration order. Default false allows TestNG reordering. Set true when order matters within a test block. Conflicts with parallel execution where threads run concurrently regardless of declared order.

Interviewer expects: When preserve-order matters vs parallel conflicts.

Q63: How do you combine groups with parallel execution?

Answer: Define groups on @Test. XML groups run include/exclude within parallel suite. Parallel methods with group filter runs matching methods concurrently. Ensure thread-safe setup for all methods in the group. Different groups can be in different test blocks.

Interviewer expects: Group filtering works alongside parallel execution.

Q64: What is the TestNG HTML report structure?

Answer: test-output/index.html: main dashboard. emailable-report.html: single-page email summary. testng-results.xml: machine-readable for CI. Failed tests show stack traces with expected vs actual. Custom listeners generate ExtentReports or Allure alongside defaults.

Interviewer expects: Know where to find failure details in CI.

Q65: How do you integrate ExtentReports with TestNG?

Answer: Implement ITestListener: onTestStart creates ExtentTest, onTestFailure adds screenshot. Initialize ExtentReports in @BeforeSuite, flush in @AfterSuite. Register listener in testng.xml. Provides dashboard with charts and tags. Alternative: Allure with @Step and @Attachment.

Interviewer expects: Listener-based reporting integration pattern.

Advanced (35)

Q66: How do you design a TestNG automation framework from scratch?

Answer: Layer architecture: Test Layer (TestNG/Cucumber) → Business Layer (Step Definitions) → Page Object Layer → Utility Layer (DriverFactory, ConfigReader) → Reporting Layer (Listeners). Separate testng XML suites per environment. Externalize config in properties files. Use Factory pattern for driver creation. Maven multi-module for large projects.

Interviewer expects: Clean layered architecture diagram explanation.

Q67: What is a hybrid framework with TestNG?

Answer: Combines Keyword-Driven (action keywords in Excel/JSON), Data-Driven (DataProvider/Excel), and POM. TestNG orchestrates execution. Cucumber adds BDD layer on top. Utilities handle driver, config, reporting. Hybrid maximizes reusability — change test data without code changes. Common in enterprise with mixed skill teams.

Interviewer expects: Explain how layers interact, not just define hybrid.

Q68: How do you achieve thread safety in parallel TestNG tests?

Answer: ThreadLocal WebDriver, ThreadLocal test data, no static mutable state, synchronized access to shared resources only when necessary, independent test data per thread, separate browser profiles. Avoid static counters, static lists, shared Page Object state. Review code for race conditions before enabling parallel.

Interviewer expects: Specific patterns: ThreadLocal, no static shared state.

Q69: What are common parallel execution failures in TestNG?

Answer: Shared WebDriver across threads, static test data modified by one thread, file write conflicts in reports, database record collisions using same user, race conditions in @BeforeClass setup, port conflicts in API tests. Fix: ThreadLocal, unique test data per thread, synchronized report writers, UUID-based test users.

Interviewer expects: Real debugging experience with parallel failures.

Q70: How do you implement custom TestNG reporter?

Answer: Implement IReporter interface. generateReport() receives List and List after all tests complete. Parse results, generate custom HTML/JSON/CSV. Register in testng.xml listeners. Access pass/fail/skip counts, duration, exception details. Can merge with ExtentReports data for unified dashboard.

Interviewer expects: IReporter generateReport implementation awareness.

Q71: What is IInvokedMethodListener?

Answer: IInvokedMethodListener provides beforeInvocation and afterInvocation callbacks for every configuration and test method. More granular than ITestListener. Use for method-level timing, logging, custom annotations processing. Access ITestResult in afterInvocation for pass/fail status of each method including @BeforeMethod.

Interviewer expects: Granular method-level hook knowledge.

Q72: What is IAlterSuiteListener?

Answer: IAlterSuiteListener.alter() modifies XmlSuite before execution starts. Programmatically add/remove tests, change parallel settings, inject listeners based on environment. Use case: CI reads git diff and adds only affected test classes to suite. Advanced dynamic test selection without maintaining multiple XML files.

Interviewer expects: Dynamic suite modification for smart CI test selection.

Q73: How do you implement TestNG with Spring dependency injection?

Answer: Use spring-test dependency. @ContextConfiguration loads Spring context. @Autowired injects page objects or services into test classes. @BeforeClass starts context. Useful when tests need real service beans or database repositories. Less common in UI automation, more in integration/API test projects.

Interviewer expects: Awareness of DI in test projects.

Q74: What is TestNG XML suite file parameterization for CI/CD?

Answer: Maven profiles swap suite XML per environment: dev-smoke.xml, staging-regression.xml, prod-sanity.xml. Jenkins parameters select profile. Resource filtering replaces ${env.url} placeholders. Single framework codebase, multiple execution configurations. Parameterized pipeline: ENV, SUITE, BROWSER, THREAD_COUNT.

Interviewer expects: Multi-environment CI strategy with TestNG.

Q75: How do you handle test data management in TestNG frameworks?

Answer: Strategy: JSON/Excel via DataProvider, API-based test data creation in @BeforeMethod, DB seeding scripts, Faker library for random data, cleanup in @AfterMethod. Central TestDataManager class. Environment-specific data in separate folders. Never hardcode credentials — use CI secrets or vault.

Interviewer expects: Complete test data lifecycle: create, use, cleanup.

Q76: What is the Page Factory pattern with TestNG?

Answer: Page Factory initializes @FindBy elements via PageFactory.initElements(driver, this) in Page Object constructor. Lazy initialization of WebElements. Works with @BeforeMethod driver setup. Limitation: stale elements in dynamic pages — prefer explicit waits over Page Factory for AJAX-heavy apps. Still widely used in enterprise frameworks.

Interviewer expects: Page Factory pros/cons with dynamic web apps.

Q77: How do you implement cross-platform test execution with TestNG?

Answer: Use Selenium Grid or cloud providers (BrowserStack, Sauce Labs). testng.xml with parallel tests for each browser/OS combo. Capabilities pattern: DesiredCapabilities or Options classes. @Parameters or @Factory for browser/OS matrix. Docker containers for consistent environments. Cloud for device/browser diversity.

Interviewer expects: Grid/cloud integration architecture.

Q78: What is TestNG method interceptor?

Answer: IMethodInterceptor intercepts test method list before execution. intercept() receives List and ITestContext, returns modified list. Use for: filtering methods by custom logic, reordering, skipping based on runtime conditions. More powerful than groups for dynamic method selection.

Interviewer expects: Dynamic method filtering beyond groups/tags.

Q79: How do you log TestNG execution with Log4j2/SLF4J?

Answer: Add Log4j2 dependency. Logger logger = LogFactory.getLogger(getClass()). Log in @BeforeMethod, test methods, listeners. log4j2.xml configures appenders: console, rolling file. Listener logs test start/end with thread name for parallel debugging. Correlation ID per test for tracing in distributed systems.

Interviewer expects: Structured logging for parallel test debugging.

Q80: What is testng-failed.xml generation?

Answer: TestNG auto-generates testng-failed.xml containing only failed tests after suite run. Re-run failures: mvn test -DsuiteXmlFile=test-output/testng-failed.xml. CI can auto-trigger failure re-run stage. Also use surefire rerunFailingTestsCount for immediate retry without separate XML.

Interviewer expects: Failure re-run strategy in CI pipelines.

Q81: How do you measure TestNG test execution performance?

Answer: ITestListener records start/end timestamps per test. IInvokedMethodListener for method-level timing. Report slow tests exceeding threshold. Maven profiler or custom dashboard. Track trends over CI builds. Identify tests exceeding timeOut threshold. Optimize waits and setup/teardown for slow tests.

Interviewer expects: Performance monitoring and optimization approach.

Q82: What is TestNG distributed testing?

Answer: Run TestNG suites across multiple machines via Selenium Grid. Hub receives tests, nodes execute on different machines/browsers. CI agents each run portion of suite. TestNG parallel + Grid node capacity. Cloud services distribute across data centers. Requires synchronized reporting aggregation.

Interviewer expects: Grid architecture for scale beyond single machine.

Q83: How do you version-control testng.xml suites?

Answer: Store in src/test/resources/suites/. Separate smoke, regression, sanity XML files. Git branch strategy: feature branches run smoke, main runs regression. Code review for suite changes like code review. Document suite purpose in XML comments. Don't commit environment-specific credentials.

Interviewer expects: Suite management as code practice.

Q84: What is the role of @Contract annotation in TestNG context?

Answer: While @Contract is not a core TestNG annotation, framework design uses interface contracts between layers. TestNG tests verify behavioral contracts. In advanced frameworks, custom annotations with IAnnotationTransformer enforce team conventions like @RequiresLogin, @CleanupData processed at runtime.

Interviewer expects: Framework governance via custom annotations.

Q85: How do you handle authentication state in TestNG UI tests?

Answer: API login to get token/cookie, inject via Selenium cookie or localStorage before UI navigation. @BeforeMethod login via API (fast) vs UI (slow). Store session in ThreadLocal. @AfterMethod logout/cleanup. Avoid UI login in every test — use API shortcut for speed.

Interviewer expects: API-based test setup for faster execution.

Q86: What is TestNG and Cucumber integration architecture?

Answer: AbstractTestNGCucumberTests as runner base class. Cucumber handles feature execution; TestNG handles suite/parallel/listeners. testng.xml runs Cucumber runner classes. Best of both: Gherkin readability + TestNG parallel and reporting. Glue code in step definitions, hooks for driver lifecycle.

Interviewer expects: Hybrid runner architecture explanation.

Q87: How do you implement environment-specific TestNG configuration?

Answer: config.properties with env suffix: config-dev.properties, config-staging.properties. @BeforeSuite reads -Denv system property, loads matching file. testng.xml parameters overridden per environment. Jenkins credentials inject secrets. Never store prod passwords in properties files committed to git.

Interviewer expects: Environment config without hardcoded secrets.

Q88: What is failure analysis strategy in TestNG CI pipelines?

Answer: Capture screenshot, page source, browser logs, network HAR on failure via listener. Classify failures: automation bug, application bug, environment issue, flaky test. Track flaky rate per test over 10 runs. Auto-create Jira on new failures. Retry then quarantine persistently flaky tests.

Interviewer expects: Mature failure triage process.

Q89: How do you implement test coverage gates with TestNG?

Answer: Parse testng-results.xml in CI: fail build if pass rate below threshold or critical test fails. JaCoCo for code coverage of test code itself. Track test count trends. Block merge if smoke suite fails. Quality gate: 95% pass rate, zero P1 test failures.

Interviewer expects: Quality gate integration in CI/CD.

Q90: What is the Object Factory pattern in TestNG?

Answer: IObjectFactory creates test class instances.custom factory injects dependencies, reads config before instantiation. @ObjectFactory on method returning ITestObjectFactory implementation. Advanced use: create test instances with different configurations from same class. Rare in standard automation but useful in large frameworks.

Interviewer expects: Advanced TestNG extensibility knowledge.

Q91: How do you test microservices with TestNG?

Answer: API tests with REST Assured + TestNG. Contract tests with Pact. Each microservice has dedicated test class/suite. @BeforeClass sets service-specific base URL. TestNG groups tag service ownership. Parallel execution per service. Integration tests verify cross-service flows. Mock external dependencies.

Interviewer expects: Microservice test strategy beyond UI automation.

Q92: What is TestNG suite thread pool tuning?

Answer: Start thread-count at CPU cores. Monitor CPU, memory, browser process count. Grid: match thread-count to available nodes. Too many threads: OOM, browser crashes, DB connection exhaustion. Profile execution: if CPU under 50%, increase threads. Document optimal settings per suite in README.

Interviewer expects: Empirical tuning methodology.

Q93: How do you implement database cleanup in TestNG?

Answer: @AfterMethod deletes test-created records using JDBC. @AfterSuite truncates test schema. Unique identifiers (UUID) per test for targeted cleanup. Transaction rollback pattern for DB tests. Never cleanup in @BeforeMethod — previous test data may still be needed for debugging failures.

Interviewer expects: Cleanup strategy preventing test data pollution.

Q94: What is the test pyramid strategy with TestNG?

Answer: 70% unit/API tests (fast, TestNG + REST Assured), 20% integration tests, 10% UI E2E (Selenium + TestNG/Cucumber). Multiple testng.xml suites per layer. CI: unit on every commit, E2E nightly. TestNG groups enforce pyramid: many @api tests, few @e2e tests.

Interviewer expects: Test pyramid applied to suite organization.

Q95: How do you migrate from JUnit to TestNG?

Answer: Replace @BeforeEach with @BeforeMethod, @Test stays similar. Add testng.xml for suite config. Update assertions from org.junit to org.testng. Maven: swap junit for testng dependency, configure surefire. Parallel execution gains immediate benefit. Cucumber runner: switch to AbstractTestNGCucumberTests.

Interviewer expects: Practical migration steps and annotation mapping.

Q96: What is TestNG best practice for 4+ years experience?

Answer: Independent tests, ThreadLocal drivers, Page Object Model, externalized config, listener-based reporting, minimal dependsOnMethods, meaningful groups, CI integration, regular flaky test cleanup, code review for test code, data cleanup after tests, API setup over UI setup.

Interviewer expects: Senior-level quality standards for test automation.

Q97: How do you debug TestNG tests in CI that pass locally?

Answer: Compare: browser version, screen resolution, timing, test data, environment config, parallel vs sequential. Enable verbose TestNG logging. Capture screenshots and logs in CI. Run CI Docker image locally. Check thread-safety issues appearing only under parallel CI load.

Interviewer expects: Systematic local vs CI debugging approach.

Q98: What is TestNG and Allure reporting integration?

Answer: Add allure-testng dependency. @Step annotates methods appearing in report. @Attachment adds screenshots. allure.properties configures results directory. Generate: allure serve target/allure-results. Integrates with TestNG lifecycle automatically. Rich timeline, categories, severity tags.

Interviewer expects: Allure as modern reporting alternative.

Q99: How do you implement security testing in TestNG framework?

Answer: OWASP ZAP integration via API. Test authentication bypass, SQL injection in input fields, XSS payloads. @Test(groups="security") runs separately from functional. Never run destructive security tests against production. Store security test payloads in dedicated data files.

Interviewer expects: Security test separation and safe execution.

Q100: What is your approach to TestNG framework maintenance?

Answer: Monthly: review flaky tests, update dependencies, archive obsolete tests. Quarterly: refactor duplicated page objects, optimize slow tests. Version pin Selenium/TestNG in pom.xml. Automated dependency update PRs with smoke validation. Documentation in Confluence/README. Deprecation policy for old test patterns.

Interviewer expects: Long-term framework ownership mindset.

Top 100 Cucumber Questions

Basic (30)

Q1: What is Cucumber?

Answer: Cucumber is a BDD tool that executes plain-text Gherkin specifications as automated tests. Bridges business and technical teams through readable feature files. Supports Java, JavaScript, Ruby, and more. Integrates with Selenium, REST Assured, and TestNG/JUnit. Living documentation that stays synced with code via step definitions.

Interviewer expects: BDD value proposition beyond just a testing tool.

Q2: What is BDD?

Answer: Behavior-Driven Development describes software behavior in natural language before coding. Uses Given-When-Then format. Encourages collaboration between business, developers, and QA (Three Amigos). Tests become specification. Cucumber is the most popular BDD framework for JVM. BDD is a process; Cucumber is a tool.

Interviewer expects: Process vs tool distinction.

Q3: What is a feature file?

Answer: A .feature file written in Gherkin describing application behavior. Contains Feature, Background, Scenarios, and Steps. Readable by non-technical stakeholders. One feature file per functionality area. Stored in src/test/resources/features/. Parsed by Cucumber runner at execution time.

Interviewer expects: Feature file structure and location in project.

Q4: What are Gherkin keywords?

Answer: Feature (description), Background (common preconditions), Scenario (test case), Scenario Outline (parameterized), Examples (data table), Given (precondition), When (action), Then (assertion), And/But (additional steps), Rule (business rule grouping in Gherkin 6+).

Interviewer expects: All keywords with purpose.

Q5: What is a step definition?

Answer: Java method annotated with @Given, @When, or @Then matching Gherkin step text. Links readable Gherkin to executable code. Multiple scenarios can reuse same step definition. Located in glue package specified in @CucumberOptions. Undefined steps fail at runtime or dryRun.

Interviewer expects: Connection between Gherkin and Java code.

Q6: What is glue code in Cucumber?

Answer: Glue is the package containing step definitions and hooks. Specified in @CucumberOptions(glue = "com.steps"). Cucumber scans glue packages for matching step definitions. Multiple glue packages allowed. Glue must be on classpath. Missing glue causes undefined step failures.

Interviewer expects: Glue package configuration.

Q7: What is a Cucumber runner class?

Answer: Java class with @CucumberOptions annotation specifying features, glue, tags, plugins. Extends AbstractTestNGCucumberTests (TestNG) or uses @RunWith(Cucumber.class) (JUnit). Entry point for Cucumber execution. Maven/IDE runs this class to execute feature files.

Interviewer expects: Runner class as test entry point.

Q8: What is @CucumberOptions?

Answer: Annotation configuring Cucumber execution: features path, glue packages, tags filter, plugins for reporting, monochrome console output, dryRun for validation, publish for Cucumber Cloud reports. Applied on runner class. All Cucumber execution settings centralized here.

Interviewer expects: Key attributes: features, glue, tags, plugin.

Q9: What is dryRun in Cucumber?

Answer: @CucumberOptions(dryRun = true) validates that every Gherkin step has a matching step definition without executing tests. Returns undefined steps list. Use before committing new scenarios to verify step coverage. Speeds up development — catch missing steps in seconds.

Interviewer expects: Development workflow use of dryRun.

Q10: What is a Scenario in Cucumber?

Answer: A Scenario is a single executable test case with Given-When-Then steps. Represents one concrete example of feature behavior. Independent execution unit in reports. Can have tags for filtering. Background steps prepended automatically before each scenario in the feature.

Interviewer expects: Scenario as atomic test unit.

Q11: What is Background in Cucumber?

Answer: Background runs before every Scenario in the feature file. Contains common Given/When steps like navigation and login. Avoids repeating same setup steps. Keep Background minimal — only truly universal preconditions. Heavy setup in Background slows every scenario.

Interviewer expects: DRY principle for common preconditions.

Q12: What is Scenario Outline?

Answer: Scenario Outline runs same scenario with multiple data sets via Examples table. Placeholders in steps matched to Examples columns. One step definition handles all rows. Ideal for testing multiple input combinations. Each row generates separate scenario in report.

Interviewer expects: Parameterized testing with Examples table.

Q13: What are Examples in Scenario Outline?

Answer: Examples table provides data rows for Scenario Outline. Header row maps column names to placeholders. Each data row executes as separate scenario. Can have multiple Example sets with different tags. Empty cells passed as empty strings to step definitions.

Interviewer expects: Examples table syntax and reporting behavior.

Q14: What are Cucumber tags?

Answer: Tags (@smoke, @regression) label scenarios or features for selective execution. Filter via @CucumberOptions(tags = "@smoke"). Tag expressions: and, or, not. Tags on Feature apply to all scenarios unless overridden. Primary mechanism for CI suite selection in Cucumber.

Interviewer expects: Tag expression syntax fluency.

Q15: What is the difference between Scenario and Scenario Outline?

Answer: Scenario has hardcoded values — one execution. Scenario Outline uses placeholders and Examples for multiple data-driven executions. Same step definitions serve both. Use Scenario for single path; Scenario Outline for data variations. Outline generates N scenarios from N data rows.

Interviewer expects: When to choose each format.

Q16: How do you write a Given step?

Answer: Given sets preconditions: Given I am logged in as "admin". Step definition: @Given("I am logged in as {string}") public void login(String role). Performs setup actions. Should be idempotent — running twice shouldn't break state. Keep Given focused on state, not actions.

Interviewer expects: Given = precondition/setup pattern.

Q17: How do you write a When step?

Answer: When describes the action: When I click the submit button. Step definition performs the interaction. One When per action for clarity. Multiple Whens allowed with And. When triggers the behavior being tested. Should not contain assertions.

Interviewer expects: When = action, no assertions rule.

Q18: How do you write a Then step?

Answer: Then verifies outcomes: Then I should see "Success" message. Step definition contains assertions. Assert on visible UI state, API response, or DB record. Multiple Thens with And for multiple validations. Then is where test pass/fail is determined.

Interviewer expects: Then = assertion/verification pattern.

Q19: What is And and But in Gherkin?

Answer: And continues the previous step type — And after Given is still a precondition. But adds negative/contrast condition. Improves readability over repeating Given/When/Then. Cucumber treats And/But identically to the preceding keyword type.

Interviewer expects: And/But as readability helpers.

Q20: What is Cucumber pretty plugin?

Answer: plugin = "pretty" formats console output with colored steps, scenario names, and pass/fail indicators. Standard for local development. Shows step duration. Does not produce file output — use html or json plugins for reports. Always include pretty for developer experience.

Interviewer expects: Console reporting during development.

Q21: What is Cucumber HTML report?

Answer: plugin = "html:target/cucumber-report.html" generates HTML report with scenario results, step details, tags, and duration. Self-contained file viewable in browser. Attach to Jira bugs. Basic but sufficient for small teams. ExtentReports/Allure provide richer alternatives.

Interviewer expects: HTML report generation and usage.

Q22: What is Cucumber JSON report?

Answer: plugin = "json:target/cucumber.json" produces JSON for CI integration. Consumed by Allure, Jenkins Cucumber Report plugin, custom dashboards. Contains feature/scenario/step hierarchy with status and duration. Essential for enterprise reporting pipelines.

Interviewer expects: JSON report for CI tool integration.

Q23: How do you run a single feature file?

Answer: Specify path in @CucumberOptions(features = "src/test/resources/features/login.feature"). Or Maven: -Dcucumber.features=path/to/feature. Run single scenario with tags: tags = "@specificTag". IDE: right-click feature file → Run. Useful for developing new scenarios.

Interviewer expects: Single feature/scenario execution methods.

Q24: What is undefined step in Cucumber?

Answer: Gherkin step with no matching step definition. Cucumber reports UndefinedStepException. dryRun=true catches before execution. Fix: create step definition with matching text or regex. Snippet generated in console suggesting step definition skeleton. Common during initial scenario writing.

Interviewer expects: How to resolve undefined steps quickly.

Q25: What is duplicate step definition error?

Answer: Two step definitions match the same Gherkin step text. Cucumber throws DuplicateStepDefinitionException at startup. Fix: remove duplicate, make patterns more specific, or use different wording in Gherkin. Regular code review of step definitions prevents duplicates.

Interviewer expects: Prevention and resolution of ambiguous steps.

Q26: What is Cucumber-JVM?

Answer: Cucumber-JVM is the Java implementation of Cucumber. Maven dependency: io.cucumber artifacts (cucumber-java, cucumber-testng). Version 7.x is current. Supports Java 11+. Replaces older info.cucumber (Cucumber 1-4) packages. Modular: core, java, testng, junit, spring.

Interviewer expects: Modern cucumber-jvm dependency coordinates.

Q27: How does Cucumber match steps to definitions?

Answer: Cucumber compares Gherkin step text against @Given/@When/@Then patterns. Supports Cucumber Expressions ({string}, {int}) and Regular Expressions. Exact match first, then pattern match. Most specific pattern wins. Ambiguous matches cause DuplicateStepDefinitionException.

Interviewer expects: Matching algorithm awareness.

Q28: What is a Cucumber Expression?

Answer: Modern step pattern syntax: {string}, {int}, {float}, {word}, {bigdecimal}. Optional text: cucumber(s). Custom parameters with regex. Preferred over pure regex for readability. Example: @When("I add {int} items") matches "I add 5 items".

Interviewer expects: Cucumber Expressions vs legacy regex.

Q29: What is the Feature keyword description?

Answer: Feature: title on first line, description lines below provide context. Feature groups related scenarios. Feature-level tags apply to all child scenarios. Not executable itself — organizational unit. Write from user perspective: "As a [role], I want [goal], so that [benefit]".

Interviewer expects: User story format in Feature description.

Q30: What is Cucumber reporting in CI?

Answer: Generate json + html plugins. Jenkins Cucumber Reports plugin parses JSON for trend graphs. Allure: io.qameta.allure.cucumber7-jvm dependency. Publish reports as build artifacts. Tag-based suite selection in CI parameters. Fail build on undefined or failed scenarios.

Interviewer expects: CI reporting pipeline with Cucumber.

Intermediate (35)

Q31: What are Cucumber hooks?

Answer: Hooks are methods with @Before, @After, @BeforeStep, @AfterStep annotations. @Before runs before each scenario; @After runs after regardless of pass/fail. Use for WebDriver init/quit, screenshot capture, test data setup. Tagged hooks @Before("@ui") run only for matching scenarios. Hooks live in glue package alongside step definitions.

Interviewer expects: Driver lifecycle in hooks, not in every step definition.

Q32: How do you use tagged hooks?

Answer: @Before("@smoke and not @api") public void beforeSmoke(Scenario s) { }. Tag expression syntax same as runner tags. Multiple tags supported. Use for browser setup per tag, API auth for @api scenarios only. Avoid too many tagged hooks — increases complexity. Document hook-tag mapping in framework README.

Interviewer expects: Selective setup/teardown based on scenario tags.

Q33: What are Data Tables in Cucumber?

Answer: Data Tables pass structured tabular data to step definitions. In Gherkin: | name | email | followed by rows. Java: DataTable parameter, or List> for header-keyed rows. Use for form filling, expected result comparison, API payload construction. DataTable.asMaps() converts to list of maps.

Interviewer expects: List conversion and form-filling use case.

Q34: How do you convert Data Tables to POJOs?

Answer: Use @DataTableType annotation on a method: @DataTableType def User user(Map row) { return new User(row.get("name")); }. Step def accepts List. Cleaner than manual map parsing. Register in glue package. Cucumber 7+ supports default data table converters.

Interviewer expects: Custom type registration for type-safe tables.

Q35: What is Scenario Context in hooks?

Answer: Scenario scenario parameter in @Before/@After provides: getName(), getId(), getSourceTagNames(), getLine(), isFailed(). Use getName() for screenshot filenames. getSourceTagNames() for conditional logic. Attach text/screenshot: scenario.attach(bytes, "image/png", "Screenshot"). Available in Cucumber 7+.

Interviewer expects: Scenario metadata for reporting and debugging.

Q36: What are Doc Strings in Cucumber?

Answer: Triple-quoted text block in Gherkin passed as String to step definition. Used for JSON payloads, long text input, expected content. Example: When I submit JSON: """{"name":"John"}""". Step: @When("I submit JSON:") public void submit(String json). Alternative to inline strings for multiline content.

Interviewer expects: Multiline string parameter for API payloads.

Q37: How do you implement custom Cucumber parameters?

Answer: Custom ParameterType: @ParameterType("(\\d+)px") public int pixel(String px) { return Integer.parseInt(px.replace("px","")); }. Use in step: @Then("width should be {pixel}"). Transforms matched text to custom type. Register in glue package. Reduces regex complexity in step definitions.

Interviewer expects: ParameterType annotation for domain-specific types.

Q38: What is Cucumber timeline report?

Answer: plugin = "timeline:target/timeline" generates HTML timeline showing scenario execution chronologically. Visualizes parallel execution, identifies bottlenecks. Each thread shown as separate row. Useful for optimizing parallel Cucumber runs. Open target/timeline/index.html after execution.

Interviewer expects: Performance analysis of parallel scenario execution.

Q39: What is rerun plugin in Cucumber?

Answer: plugin = "rerun:target/rerun.txt" writes failed scenario paths to file. Re-run only failures: mvn test -Dcucumber.features=@target/rerun.txt. Speeds up CI failure feedback loop. Combine with retry in hooks for flaky scenarios. Standard practice in mature CI pipelines.

Interviewer expects: Failure-only re-execution strategy.

Q40: How do you organize feature files?

Answer: One feature per application module: login.feature, checkout.feature. Group related scenarios under one Feature keyword. Place in src/test/resources/features/ mirroring app structure. Avoid mega feature files with 50+ scenarios. Use subdirectories: features/api/, features/ui/. Consistent naming: verb-noun.feature.

Interviewer expects: Feature file organization mirroring application modules.

Q41: How do you reuse steps across features?

Answer: Same step text in multiple features maps to one step definition. Design reusable, generic steps: "I am logged in as {string}" not "I login with admin credentials". Shared step definition classes in common glue package. Avoid duplicate step definitions with slightly different wording.

Interviewer expects: Reusable generic step design philosophy.

Q42: What is declarative vs imperative Gherkin?

Answer: Declarative: "Given I am logged in" (what, not how). Imperative: "Given I click login button and enter user and pass" (how). Declarative is BDD best practice — readable by business. Implementation details hidden in step definitions. Imperative Gherkin becomes unmaintainable as UI changes.

Interviewer expects: Strong preference for declarative style with examples.

Q43: How do you handle waits in Cucumber steps?

Answer: Use explicit WebDriverWait inside step definitions or Page Objects — never Thread.sleep. Wrap in page object methods: wait.until(ExpectedConditions.visibilityOfElementLocated(locator)). Keep Gherkin free of wait language. Centralize timeout values in config.properties. Log wait timeouts for debugging slow pages.

Interviewer expects: Explicit waits in page objects, not Gherkin or sleep.

Q44: How do you take screenshots in Cucumber?

Answer: @After hook: if (scenario.isFailed()) { byte[] screenshot = ((TakesScreenshot)driver).getScreenshotAs(OutputType.BYTES); scenario.attach(screenshot, "image/png", scenario.getName()); }. Works with Allure and Cucumber native reports. Also capture on @AfterStep for step-level debugging.

Interviewer expects: Hook-based screenshot on failure pattern.

Q45: What is Cucumber strict mode?

Answer: In older versions, strict=true failed suite on pending/undefined steps. Cucumber 7 treats undefined steps as errors by default. Use dryRun=true during development to catch undefined steps. In CI, any undefined step should fail the build immediately.

Interviewer expects: Zero tolerance for undefined steps in CI.

Q46: How do you test negative scenarios in Cucumber?

Answer: Write explicit negative scenarios: Scenario: Login with invalid password. Then step verifies error message. Use Examples table for multiple invalid inputs. Tag @negative for separate CI execution. Don't mix positive and negative in same scenario — one behavior per scenario.

Interviewer expects: Dedicated negative scenarios with clear Then assertions.

Q47: What is the Rule keyword in Gherkin?

Answer: Rule groups scenarios under a business rule. Feature: Password Policy / Rule: Minimum 8 characters / Scenario: Valid password. Improves organization in complex features. Optional — not all teams use it. Supported in Gherkin 6+. Scenarios under a Rule inherit its context.

Interviewer expects: Business rule grouping in feature files.

Q48: How do you run Cucumber from Maven with tags?

Answer: mvn test -Dcucumber.filter.tags="@smoke and not @wip". Override features: -Dcucumber.features=path/to/feature. Override glue: -Dcucumber.glue=com.steps. Configure defaults in @CucumberOptions on runner class. Jenkins parameterizes tag expression per build type.

Interviewer expects: Maven command-line tag filtering for CI.

Q49: What is monochrome in @CucumberOptions?

Answer: monochrome=true removes ANSI color codes from console output. Useful for CI logs that don't support colors. Output is plain text — easier to parse in Jenkins console. Keep pretty plugin for local development with colors. Set monochrome=true in CI runner configuration.

Interviewer expects: CI-friendly console output configuration.

Q50: How do you handle multiple environments in Cucumber?

Answer: ConfigReader loads properties based on -Denv system property. @Before hook reads env and sets base URL. Environment-specific feature files rarely needed — same features, different config. Jenkins injects env-specific credentials. Never hardcode URLs in feature files or step definitions.

Interviewer expects: Environment config externalization pattern.

Q51: What is snippet generation?

Answer: When Cucumber finds undefined steps, console prints suggested step definition skeletons. snippets=CamelCase or PASCALCASE controls method naming. Use during development: run with dryRun=false, copy snippets, implement methods. Speeds up step definition creation.

Interviewer expects: Development workflow using snippet output.

Q52: How do you validate API responses in Cucumber steps?

Answer: Use REST Assured in @Then steps: response.then().statusCode(200).body("name", equalTo("John")). Store Response in scenario-scoped variable via PicoContainer or instance field. Separate API steps from UI steps using @api tag. API steps should not reference WebDriver.

Interviewer expects: REST Assured integration in Then steps.

Q53: What is conditional execution in Cucumber?

Answer: Tagged hooks for conditional setup. ITestContext or static flags for runtime decisions. Skip scenario: throw new PendingException("Feature not ready") — marks pending/skipped. @Before hook checks environment availability and throws exception to skip. Prefer tag-based filtering over runtime skipping.

Interviewer expects: Tag-based filtering preferred over runtime skip.

Q54: How do you share state between step definitions?

Answer: PicoContainer DI (cucumber-picocontainer dependency): shared classes auto-injected into step def constructors. Instance fields in same step def class for multi-step scenarios. Scenario Context via custom World object. Never use static fields for WebDriver in parallel — use ThreadLocal.

Interviewer expects: PicoContainer for shared state between steps.

Q55: What is Cucumber 7 migration from older versions?

Answer: Package change: io.cucumber replaces cucumber.api. Update imports in step defs and hooks. junit-vintage removed — use junit-platform or TestNG. Message protocol replaces old formatter API. Update pom.xml: io.cucumber:cucumber-java:7.x, cucumber-testng:7.x. Run dryRun to verify all steps still match.

Interviewer expects: io.cucumber package migration knowledge.

Q56: How do you integrate Cucumber with Spring?

Answer: cucumber-spring dependency. @CucumberContextConfiguration on Spring config class. @Autowired beans into step definitions. Spring manages test context lifecycle. Useful for integration tests needing Spring beans, DB repositories, or service layer. @Before hook can @Autowired WebDriver bean.

Interviewer expects: Spring context in step definitions for integration tests.

Q57: What is feature-level vs scenario-level tags?

Answer: Feature-level tag applies to all scenarios in feature unless scenario has overriding tag. @smoke on Feature tags every scenario. Scenario-level tag adds to feature tags. Tag inheritance: scenario tags = feature tags + own tags. Use feature tags for module-wide categorization.

Interviewer expects: Tag inheritance from feature to scenarios.

Q58: How do you name scenarios properly?

Answer: Name describes behavior and expected outcome: "Successful login with valid credentials" not "Test 1". Include business context. Avoid technical terms in names. Scenario Outline: name describes pattern: "Login fails with ". Consistent naming helps report readability and failure triage.

Interviewer expects: Business-readable scenario naming convention.

Q59: What is the pickle runner in Cucumber?

Answer: Pickle is internal Cucumber representation of executable scenario (compiled from AST). Each Example row creates separate Pickle. Understanding Pickles helps debug parallel execution and report mapping. Not directly exposed to users but referenced in advanced parallel configuration.

Interviewer expects: Internal scenario representation awareness.

Q60: How do you handle authentication in Cucumber?

Answer: Fast approach: API login in @Before hook, inject token/cookie into browser. UI login as dedicated scenario for login feature only. Store auth state in PicoContainer shared context. @Before("@authenticated") hook performs login. @After hook clears session. Never login via UI in every scenario.

Interviewer expects: API-based auth setup in hooks for speed.

Q61: What is cucumber-junit-platform-engine?

Answer: Cucumber 7 JUnit 5 integration via junit-platform-engine. Alternative to AbstractTestNGCucumberTests. Use @Suite with @SelectClasspathResource for JUnit 5. Better IDE integration with JUnit 5. TestNG still preferred in enterprise Selenium projects for parallel and listener features.

Interviewer expects: Awareness of JUnit 5 vs TestNG runner options.

Q62: How do you lint Gherkin files?

Answer: Use gherkin-lint npm tool or review checklist: max 10 steps per scenario, no And as first step, declarative language, consistent Given-When-Then. CI can run gherkin-lint as pre-commit hook. Prevents feature file quality degradation over time.

Interviewer expects: Gherkin quality enforcement in CI.

Q63: What is the difference between Cucumber and SpecFlow?

Answer: Cucumber-JVM for Java/Kotlin. SpecFlow for .NET/C#. Both use Gherkin syntax. SpecFlow integrates with Visual Studio and Reqnroll (successor). Cucumber has larger Java community. Same BDD principles apply. Choose based on technology stack.

Interviewer expects: Tool selection based on tech stack.

Q64: How do you handle file upload in Cucumber?

Answer: Step definition: driver.findElement(By.id("file")).sendKeys(absoluteFilePath). File must exist on machine running test. In CI, store test files in src/test/resources/testdata/. For remote grid, use LocalFileDetector. Never interact with OS file dialog — sendKeys to hidden input.

Interviewer expects: sendKeys file upload pattern, not OS dialog.

Q65: What is scenario-level timeout in Cucumber?

Answer: Configure via TestNG @Test(timeOut) on runner or custom @Before hook with ExecutorService and Future.get(timeout). Cucumber itself has no native scenario timeout. Wrap scenario execution or set TestNG timeout on runner class methods. Log timeout with scenario name for debugging.

Interviewer expects: Timeout via TestNG integration or custom hook.

Advanced (35)

Q66: How do you run Cucumber scenarios in parallel?

Answer: cucumber.execution.parallel.enabled=true in junit-platform.properties or @DataProvider parallel with AbstractTestNGCucumberTests. Set parallel config: cucumber.execution.parallel.config.strategy=dynamic, fixed, or custom. Each scenario runs in separate thread. Requires ThreadLocal WebDriver and independent test data. Start with 2-4 threads, scale based on CI capacity.

Interviewer expects: Parallel config properties and thread safety requirements.

Q67: What is PicoContainer in Cucumber?

Answer: cucumber-picocontainer dependency enables constructor injection in step definitions. Shared objects (DriverFactory, ApiClient) injected automatically. Scenario-scoped lifecycle — new instances per scenario. Constructor: public LoginSteps(WebDriver driver, LoginPage page). Eliminates static state. Required for parallel Cucumber execution.

Interviewer expects: Constructor injection pattern with PicoContainer.

Q68: How do you design Cucumber framework architecture?

Answer: Layers: Features → Step Definitions → Page Objects/Services → Utilities. Runner classes per suite (smoke, regression). Hooks class for driver lifecycle. PicoContainer for DI. ConfigReader for environment. Separate glue packages: steps, hooks, pages, utils. One runner per tag group in CI.

Interviewer expects: Layered architecture diagram explanation.

Q69: How do you test REST APIs with Cucumber?

Answer: REST Assured in step definitions. Given sets base URI and auth. When sends request. Then validates status and body. Service Object pattern: UserApiService wraps REST Assured calls. Tag @api for API-only scenarios. No WebDriver in API steps. Store Response in shared context.

Interviewer expects: Complete API testing layer in Cucumber framework.

Q70: How do you implement Cucumber with Selenium Grid?

Answer: @Before hook creates RemoteWebDriver with grid URL and capabilities. Pass -Dgrid.url=http://hub:4444. Parallel scenarios connect to different grid nodes. Docker Compose for local grid setup. Cloud providers (BrowserStack) as managed grid. Quit driver in @After hook to release node.

Interviewer expects: RemoteWebDriver setup in hooks for grid execution.

Q71: What is Cucumber message protocol?

Answer: Standardized event format (NDJSON) for Cucumber execution. plugin = "message:target/messages.ndjson". Consumed by Allure, custom report generators. Replaces legacy JSON formatter internals. Enables tool-agnostic report processing. Foundation for Cucumber Reports cloud service.

Interviewer expects: Modern reporting protocol awareness.

Q72: How do you publish Cucumber reports?

Answer: publish=true in @CucumberOptions uploads to Cucumber Reports cloud. Requires Cucumber CI token. Self-hosted: generate json plugin, process with Allure or Jenkins Cucumber Report plugin. Attach html report to Jira bugs. Archive reports as CI build artifacts with retention policy.

Interviewer expects: Report publishing in enterprise CI pipeline.

Q73: How do you handle dynamic data in Cucumber?

Answer: Generate at runtime in @Before hook: String email = "user_" + UUID.randomUUID() + "@test.com". Faker library for realistic data. API creates test data, UI verifies. Store generated values in PicoContainer context for later steps. Cleanup in @After hook via API or DB.

Interviewer expects: Runtime data generation with cleanup strategy.

Q74: What is shared WebDriver anti-pattern?

Answer: Static WebDriver field shared across scenarios causes failures in parallel execution. Thread A navigates while Thread B quits driver. Fix: ThreadLocal in DriverFactory, inject via PicoContainer. One driver per scenario thread. Never pass driver as static. Code review for static driver references.

Interviewer expects: Identify and fix shared driver anti-pattern.

Q75: How do you version Cucumber dependencies?

Answer: Pin io.cucumber version in pom.xml properties: 7.18.0. Align cucumber-java, cucumber-testng, cucumber-picocontainer to same version. Test with dryRun after upgrades. Watch GitHub releases for breaking changes. Automated Dependabot PRs with smoke suite validation.

Interviewer expects: Dependency version alignment strategy.

Q76: How do you test microservices with Cucumber?

Answer: Each service has feature files for its API endpoints. Shared authentication steps. Contract tests verify service interfaces. Orchestration scenarios test cross-service flows. Tag by service: @user-service, @order-service. Independent execution per service in CI. Mock external dependencies with WireMock.

Interviewer expects: Microservice BDD organization strategy.

Q77: What is Cucumber anti-pattern: long scenarios?

Answer: Scenarios with 20+ steps are unmaintainable. Split into focused scenarios with Background for shared setup. Each scenario tests one behavior. Long scenarios indicate missing abstraction in step definitions. Review feature files in PR — reject scenarios exceeding 10 steps.

Interviewer expects: Scenario length governance in code review.

Q78: How do you implement custom Cucumber plugin?

Answer: Implement ConcurrentEventListener or EventListener. Register via @CucumberOptions plugin class. Handle TestCaseStarted, TestCaseFinished events. Generate custom metrics, send to monitoring system. Advanced use case for enterprise observability integration.

Interviewer expects: Custom event listener plugin development.

Q79: What is dependency injection beyond PicoContainer?

Answer: Spring DI with cucumber-spring for Spring Boot apps. Guice with cucumber-guice. Manual DI via constructor in simple frameworks. PicoContainer is lightest for Selenium projects. Choose based on application architecture — match app's DI framework.

Interviewer expects: DI option selection rationale.

Q80: How do you handle iFrames in Cucumber?

Answer: Page Object method: driver.switchTo().frame(locator), interact, switchTo().defaultContent(). Step definition calls page object — no frame logic in Gherkin. Handle nested frames with switchTo().parentFrame(). Always return to default content in finally block to prevent context leaks.

Interviewer expects: Frame handling encapsulated in page objects.

Q81: What is Cucumber filter tags property?

Answer: System property cucumber.filter.tags overrides @CucumberOptions tags at runtime. Jenkins: mvn test -Dcucumber.filter.tags="@regression and @ui". Enables same runner for different CI jobs. Takes precedence over annotation. Supports full tag expression syntax.

Interviewer expects: Runtime tag override for CI parameterization.

Q82: How do you integrate Allure with Cucumber 7?

Answer: Dependency: io.qameta.allure:allure-cucumber7-jvm. Auto-attaches scenario results. @Step annotation on step definition methods for detailed steps in report. scenario.attach() for screenshots. Generate: allure serve target/allure-results. Rich timeline, categories, severity.

Interviewer expects: Allure + Cucumber 7 integration setup.

Q83: What is testable Gherkin review checklist?

Answer: Is it declarative? One behavior per scenario? Readable by product owner? No technical locators? Reusable steps? Proper tags? Examples cover edge cases? Background minimal? Follows team style guide? Review in Three Amigos session before automation.

Interviewer expects: Quality checklist for feature file review.

Q84: How do you handle OAuth in Cucumber?

Answer: API step obtains token via client credentials or password grant. Store token in scenario context. UI step injects cookie/localStorage. Alternatively automate OAuth UI flow in dedicated @oauth tagged scenarios. Use test OAuth server or mock authorization server. Never store real OAuth secrets in feature files.

Interviewer expects: OAuth automation strategy for test environments.

Q85: What is Cucumber execution dry-run vs runtime?

Answer: dryRun=true: validates step defs, no browser/API calls. Runtime: full execution with all hooks and steps. CI pipeline: dryRun in PR validation (fast), full run on merge. Local: dryRun when adding new scenarios, runtime for development. Combine: dryRun catches missing steps before wasting CI time.

Interviewer expects: Two-phase validation in CI pipeline.

Q86: How do you migrate from Cucumber 4 to 7?

Answer: Update pom.xml dependencies to io.cucumber 7.x. Replace cucumber.api imports with io.cucumber.java.en. Update hook imports: io.cucumber.java.Before. Replace AbstractTestNGCucumberTests import. Test EventListener API if custom plugins. Run full suite with dryRun first, then runtime.

Interviewer expects: Step-by-step migration experience.

Q87: What is World object in Cucumber?

Answer: Shared context object holding scenario state: tokens, created IDs, WebDriver reference. Instantiate via PicoContainer or @Before hook. Step definitions access World's fields. Cleaner than static variables. Pattern: public class TestContext { public String orderId; public WebDriver driver; }.

Interviewer expects: World/Context object pattern for scenario state.

Q88: How do you optimize slow Cucumber suites?

Answer: Profile with timeline report. Identify slowest scenarios. Replace UI setup with API setup. Reduce unnecessary Background steps. Parallel execution. Headless browser mode. Skip non-critical scenarios in smoke. Cache authentication tokens. Target: smoke under 10 minutes, regression under 1 hour.

Interviewer expects: Data-driven suite optimization approach.

Q89: What is BDD framework governance?

Answer: Gherkin style guide document. Feature file templates. Step definition naming conventions. PR review checklist for .feature files. Regular Three Amigos sessions. Archive obsolete scenarios. Tag strategy document. Onboarding guide for new team members. Quarterly feature file audit.

Interviewer expects: Framework governance for team scale.

Q90: How do you test GraphQL with Cucumber?

Answer: HTTP client or REST Assured with GraphQL query in request body. Step: When I query GraphQL with query "{ users { id name } }". Then validate JSON response path. Store queries in external .graphql files for complex queries. Tag @graphql for separate execution.

Interviewer expects: GraphQL testing approach in BDD framework.

Q91: What is Cucumber compatibility with JUnit 5?

Answer: cucumber-junit-platform-engine for native JUnit 5. @Suite + @IncludeEngines("cucumber"). Parallel via JUnit 5 parallel config. TestNG still more common in Selenium for ITestListener and XML suites. JUnit 5 better for Spring Boot integration test projects.

Interviewer expects: JUnit 5 vs TestNG runner selection criteria.

Q92: How do you handle database in Cucumber steps?
